i use a distro not many use in India. It is called ArchLinux.
It has a small base install which is abt 90 mb once u remove stuff like ppp
and xfs progs form the base. It s i686 optimized and so are all its packages
and it has a great package manager called pacman which  is lightning fast(
written in C). But this distro is highly dependent on a good net connection!
eg. to get xorg and openbox type
# pacman -Sy xorg openbox

I guess, it's not a general practice. CVS is a VC used for distributed
development. Why do you wish to have a file in CVS and prevent it from
updates done by other developers ? If you wish to prevent, it's also
good to have it out of the repository.

From vijaykumar at bravegnu.org  Sun Jul  2 07:08:35 2006
From: vijaykumar at bravegnu.org (Vijay Kumar)
Date: Sun Jul  2 12:45:22 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Preventing a file from being updated in CVS
References: <9a9bfc170607010420x7cb3d01fm770b947b6a2fb3d6@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <loom.20060702T090404-699@post.gmane.org>

 <R.Ramkumar> writes:

> Is it possible to prevent a file in a CVS tree from being subject to
> further updates. I would like to have a local version of those files,
> and would not like CVS to try merging or reporting conflicts on those
> files.

To hold a file in revision x.x, you can use the following command.

cvs update -r x.x <filename>

Further cvs updates will not modify the file. To get rid of the sticky revision
no. and to move to the head use the following command.

cvs update -A <filename>

Regards,
Vijay

Subject: [Ilugc] Non-Tech Discussion - Which Distro is the Best ??..
In-Reply-To: <5580629a0606302108h6234fc84r29af2ff58f723500@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d6e7f37f0606292352r5bf271bar9ba747f354c39531@mail.gmail.com>
	<5580629a0606302108h6234fc84r29af2ff58f723500@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <6be355de0607030438u57ec553fkc54d89bd01d6f910@mail.gmail.com>

Though I've tried out many distros, am a beginner to intermediate kind of
user. I find Debian Sarge, Ubuntu Dapper and Vector 5.1 equally fast on my
good old hardware and easy to use too. Infact Dapper boots much faster than
Breezy or Debian Sarge too. All 3 are equally recommendable for beginners.
Infact Ubuntu Dapper would be at the 1st place, does'nt even give you the
pain of choosing typical packages (assuming you have about 5-6 GB to
allocate for linux.

Vector...everything except I had to manually configure the boot loader from
Ubuntu's GRUB (run a Ubuntu-Vector dual boot). Thats bcos I had booting
problems, even booting Vector from the LILO Vector installed. Windoze booted
without any problems then.

-narayanan

Hi Shiv,

/me playing devil's advocate here..

On 7/3/06, Sivasankar Chander <siva.ilugc@gmail.com> wrote:
> On 7/3/06, Chakkaradeep C C <chaks.yoper@gmail.com> wrote:
> >
> >
> > http://in.rediff.com/money/2006/jul/03ms.htm
> >
> > News like these always threatens us somehow as M$ tries to capture the
> > Market by pouring MONEY....how far Linux is going to handle these...
> >
> >   Don't worry - Windows Mobile has been mostly a failure. Even the much-
> ballyhooed Palm Treo 700w, which was hailed as a transition by Palm
> away from PalmOS to Windows Mobile, has seen sales far lower than
> expected. Palm will pull the plug and move back to PalmOS (most
> probably as an app on an underlying Linux virtualizer) sooner or later.

OTOH,

The HP iPaq's (and the PocketPC line) have been hugely succesful in
the smartphone area. The Dell Axim x51 is a very good PDA if you have
multimedia needs. Palm OS based Palm LifeDrive is a huge failure.

The O2 XDA line is another good smartphone. Windows Mobile has found
it's way into multimedia players, the Toshiba Gigabeat S is a
excellent example, the UI is better than that of the iPod. HTC has
done wonders with the Mobile OS, the HTC Universal and the HTC Wizard
are great devices.

yes, there is Linux based stuff out there, Archos/iRiver (IIRC) are
huge Linux supporters, but as it stands I see Windows Mobile in the
forefront of PDA/smartphone technology.

In multimedia devices arena, Rockbox is good, but is again not backed
by any commercial vendor.

Maemo looks promising but the reviews of the Nokia 770 have not been
great. There seem to be no future commitments from Nokia on it though.
The GP2X is great again but has failed to pick up due to lack of
thrid-party support.

I'm waiting for gadgets using OpenMAX , but apart from the PS3(which
is huge) nobody else seems to bother about it.

The problem is , the FOSS world has the development environment
problem sorted out it's just that the big-fish are not biting the
bait. Motorola is an exception here, but then again they just want a
free OS which can run Java.

There is going to be a huge gap in the embedded OS space as Symbian
fails to meet requirements, and the way I see it, M$ seems to have
cornered all the players in the field to have a bite of the Windows
Mobile pie.

-Toufeeq
PS: Google for tech-jargon mentioned above ;)

blog @ http://toufeeq.blogspot.com

On 7/3/06, Toufeeq Hussain <toufeeqh@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
>
> OTOH,
>
> The HP iPaq's (and the PocketPC line) have been hugely succesful in
> the smartphone area. The Dell Axim x51 is a very good PDA if you have
> multimedia needs. Palm OS based Palm LifeDrive is a huge failure.


   Windows Mobile has overwhelming market share in PDAs, but not in
Smartphones. The thing to note is that PDAs are a shrinking market, and
cellphones are substituting them.

as it stands I see Windows Mobile in the
> forefront of PDA/smartphone technology.


    PDAs maybe; Smartphones, no. They're almost completely out of the
picture in Smartphones, except for the Treo 700w.

Maemo looks promising but the reviews of the Nokia 770 have not been
> great. There seem to be no future commitments from Nokia on it though.


Yes, according to a Nokia insider whom I met, Maemo was a learning
experiment which they're not going to follow up on.


> There is going to be a huge gap in the embedded OS space as Symbian
> fails to meet requirements, and the way I see it, M$ seems to have
> cornered all the players in the field to have a bite of the Windows
> Mobile pie.
>
>   Symbian will not go away - the Nokia Series 60 UI runs on Symbian and
some 1 billion people around the world are so familiar with it that it
cannot be easily substituted. However, a Series 60 port to Linux is
certainly possible, in which case Symbian will whither away and die.

  Windows Mobile will survive in the PDA space, but that's a small
volume niche. There isn't enough revenue in this space to support the
number of companies that are out there - some will have to pull the
plug, including HP and Dell. Only low-end Chinese manufacturers
like HTC and Vtech will survive. That's not the kind of revenue model
that M$ is looking for.

-Siva

P.S. The early Linux handhelds failed commercially, but those were
mainly PDAs. In phones, both the NTT Docomo i-mode units running
Linux as well as Motorola's Java units have sold huge numbers. The
platform standardization news that I posted is huge news, not least
because both Motorola and Docomo are involved.

Hi Arun,

--- Arun Velusamy <arunvelusamy@aim.com> wrote:
>     How can i get information on my modem device
> driver?  Its running in 
> /dev/ttyS0. 

Check for your modem/driver info in /proc if using 2.4
Linux kernel. In 2.6 Linux kernels, check /sys and
/proc.

Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
> hi,
> we are planning to buy some managed switches for our network. We got  a 
> quotation which seems exorbitant. Can anyone recommend switches/ dealers 
> in chennai for a network (fully linux), along with some idea  of the costs

unmanaged switches are dirt cheap

genuinely good managed switches are worth every paisa you pay for them, 
especially if you're on the sort of network that'll need managed ones.

poor quality managed switches have this nasty habit of falling over 
under high load, making an entire segment of IPs unreachable etc.

> Any specific FOSS in mind?

nothing specific. we are starting a major effort to get people to  
code applications in foss. So we need in house expertise in  
translation as it will be mandatory that all projects we house be  
localised at the outset (which means that there will be no button  
saying 'tamil' or 'telugu' which will say 'not yet implemented' when  
clicked). This implies that the tools they use should also be  
translated. Candidates would be things like django, pygtk, wxpython,  
various php apps, mediawiki? and the like, along with the  
applications we develop.

Subject: [Ilugc] Re: [slightly OT] managed switches
References: <D97C340D-CD73-434B-A302-068C02C64E6E@thenilgiris.com>

Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@...> writes:

> we are planning to buy some managed switches for our network. We got  
> a quotation which seems exorbitant. Can anyone recommend switches/ 
> dealers in chennai for a network (fully linux), along with some idea  
> of the costs

dont know what you think is exorbitant. unmanaged switches are typically 100 to
150 bucks per port while managed ones run about 1000 to 1500 bucks per port. it
is not just for the management capability that you pay - look at other specs
like max mac address table size etc. like srs has pointed out, cheap managed
switches and most unmanaged switches do funny and bad things under heavy load.

sriram

Dear friends,

My friend gave me the fabulous explanation of what is the similarity between
salt satyagraha and software satyagraha.

Dandi March :
The salt march was aimed to send a clearcut message to the ouster of british
regime which enforced taxes for a mineral(salt) which is available free of
cost  in the coastline.

Gundy March:
We, The foss enthusiats convey the need of  FOSS software which is available
at  free of cost, instead of taking a proprietory solution to the common man
of India.

I read the meaning of what satyagraha from

http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_March which quotes the words of  Mahatma
as

 *"Truth (Satya) implies Love, and Firmness (Agraha) engenders and therefore
serves as a synonym for force? that is to say, the Force which is born of
Truth and Love or Non-violence? [If] we are Satyagrahis and offer
Satyagraha, believing ourselves to be strong? we grow stronger and stronger
everyday. With our increase in strength, our Satyagraha too becomes more
effective, and we would never be casting about for an opportunity to give it
up."* --Gandhi
Lets give some momentum to this walk programme. members add up your views.


Thanking you,

Sincerely


Thyagarajan Shanmugham

On 7/6/06, Suresh Ramasubramanian <linux@frodo.hserus.net> wrote:
> Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
> >
> > what are the advantages of a managed switch over an unmanaged one?  Or,
> > rather, why would one need a managed switch?
> >
>
> suppose your switch is sitting in a datacenter a couple of continents
> away?  connected to a big rack of servers, pushing high amounts of
> traffic?  that's when you need managed servers.
>
> for a small office lan - go get a good unmanaged one (by which i mean
> "anything but d-link")

A managed switch is one which has an IP address assigned to itself
through which you can access its console and configure its settings.
You can setup virtual LANs - where the same switch can make it appear
that one set of nodes are on a network different from the other set
(connected to the same switch). For example you can have the nodes of
the accounts dept to be on a separate (virtual) LAN from the rest - so
tools like packet sniffers do not help trouble makers.

IMO, for LANs with upto 100 nodes unmanaged switches would be the
ideal option. When you buy a managed switch you would also have to pay
for a CCNA type to configure it properly for your network and 'manage'
it on a regular basis - what good is a managed switch if there is no
one to manage it!

regds,
mano

On 06-Jul-06, at 10:15 AM, Mano wrote:

> IMO, for LANs with upto 100 nodes unmanaged switches would be the
> ideal option. When you buy a managed switch you would also have to pay
> for a CCNA type to configure it properly for your network and 'manage'
> it on a regular basis - what good is a managed switch if there is no
> one to manage it!

we have 120 machines on our lan. From the internet, we have an 8-port  
switch. 3 lines from this go to the servers (dhcp,mail, file,  
firewall etc), 4 lines are free and *one* line goes to a 24 port  
switch to which some machines are connected directly and the rest  
through 5 hubs. We were advised that we should have the 5 lines from  
the main 8-port switch go to 5 managed switches to which all the  
machines can be connected without using hubs.

the problems we are facing with the current setup:
1. slow speed for the machines downstream
2. some machines need static IPs for various reasons. We find that  
students in the labs put these static IPs on their machines creating  
problems.

any comments?

> Slow speed :
What are the applications it is slow ( it is net browsing/download/mail etc
)
what is the os in all the systems

in my understanding most of the network clogging  problems are due to
unwanted traffic caused by viruses.
If you ensure that the virus traffic is eliminated ( ie if all are running
on Linux else have a good  antivirus) then a network with 10 / 100 mbps enet
card and a simmilar ordinary switch stack should not be the bottle neck for
a  120  system network .
if you still have  speed issues , i suggest that upgrade the net back bone
connection which  probably is the bottle neck.
If the problem still persists , them you may look at upgrading the switches.

Dear friends,

>
> would we be spreading the message to the *real* (IT users) audience with
> a public walk?
>

Some time back in the television i have seen an advertisement. It struct me
once i saw it, The  ad goes like this, Few physically challenged children
will set for a race, one of them will fell down in the middle, all the rest
of the children will turn back and come to the child and pick him up,
finally they will form a human chain by clubbing their arms and pass the
finish line.The ad ends with a caption saying "Human spirits will never be
handicapped, NEVER".

This walk is to say "This is a community driven programme" for using
computer in a free legitimate way in the  ever expanding world of
technology. We are here for helping each other in the computing world. We
are looking for the human domain whether they are raw or expertised user. We
are showing our solidarity in the world of computing. By this , it never
means we are against any proprietory company like M$windows. We say about
the might of our community.


Cheers,

Thyagarajan shanmugham

should have good experience in compiling and debugging, Experience in
drivers, Bootloader dev, Root file system development etc.

On Thu July 6 2006 9:08 pm, Suresh Ramasubramanian wrote:
> Mohammed Riyaz wrote:
> >>On 7/6/06, Prashanth Mohan <prashmohan@gmail.com> wrote:
> >>>#2. What I had intended was that the by doing `walks' it somehow takes a
> >>>political turn of events.
> >
> > I still wonder if it would serve any purpose at all.
>
> great exercise, improves your digestion etc?

1. While not opposing proprietory software, we can hold banners against 
software piracy. Promote honesty among software users. If all the proprietory 
software being used are forced to be paid for, I am sure many of the users 
will consider open source alternatives.

2. Distribute CDs containing Windows versions of Open Source alternatives. A 
CD containing Firefox, Open Office, Gaim, Thunderbird etc can be prepared and 
distributed during the walk.

3. If it is going to be a Guindy walk, we should choose a working day peak 
hour time (8 am) and target the office/college going public. On a sunday as 
pointed out we might not reach the target audience. 

4. A walk from Guindy railway station to Gandhi Mandapam will cover a lot of 
ground. Office workers commuting to Tidal Park and beyond, Students going to 
Anna University campuses, government employees going to Anna Salai and beyond 
would be potential spectators for the walk. 

Count me in for such a walk in any form. It is a great exercise and improves 
digestion :-). 

Having benefitted so much from open source software and not having contributed 
back in equal measure I feel a personal obligation to participate in such 
events. 

Best regards,

Ma Sivakumar

alternatives for their current operating system (mostly Windows), will cut 
down their dependance on proprietary applications.

large scale impact, promoting open source applications will be useful.

Hi,

You don't have to disable firewall in Linux. Just
add the incoming port number to the firewall
to allow incoming connections to the KBittorrent.

You also have to set up port forwarding in your
CPE/router to accept incoming connections.
Check this link for configuring port forwarding
in your router/CPE.
http://www.portforward.com/english/routers/port_forwarding/routerindex.htm

-Sriram K

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Fri Jul  7 17:20:06 2006
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Fri Jul  7 17:17:32 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Help on bit torrent
In-Reply-To: <dd680c2b0607061115o71f9d6f2n290545850e56c0b@mail.gmail.com>
References: <dd680c2b0607061115o71f9d6f2n290545850e56c0b@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <44AE4A6E.8000701@gmail.com>

Shrinivasan T wrote:

> In suse 10, I got a tool called KBittorrent.
> Is any direct connection to net is needed for Bittorrent?
>
> How to make it work?

BitTorrent is used to download files from the internet using peer to 
peer sharing, and it helps to reduce load on busy ftp servers and 
possibly faster downloads from a source close to you.

 From the file menu of kbittorrent, select "paste bittorrent url", and 
enter the url of the file you want to download.

For example, if you want to download the latest FreeBSD 6.1 release 
iso's, get the url from: http://torrents.freebsd.org:8080/

On Ubuntu, bittorrent may be invoked from mozilla or firefox. Using 
synaptic or other package managers, install bittorrent.Open mozilla or 
firefox.  Point the browser to a bittorrent seed. Click on the file you 
want to download, and select "open with default application 
/usr/bin/btdownloadgui " and do the rest.  man btdownloadgui for more info.

If download is interrupted, you could continue it later and manage it 
well. BitTorrent generally downloads the iso's etc into directories 
along with md5 checksums if any.  If you are using k3b to burn the iso 
to a cd, the integrity of the download is checked automatically.   HTH.
__

From chaks.yoper at gmail.com  Fri Jul  7 19:43:55 2006
From: chaks.yoper at gmail.com (Chakkaradeep C C)
Date: Fri Jul  7 19:44:04 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Linux and Users
Message-ID: <a54a308e0607070713j24e94edaxf6bb2925a33bb688@mail.gmail.com>

Hi all,

This mail is not intended to create disagreement or war. Its just for
discussion.

I see many are interested in creating awareness about FOSS and OSS (somebody
told me both are different) thru a Walk or by taking other initiatives. I
thought i should share my views.

The first audience for these kinda awareness programs are The People.When i
say People, it includes all types of People.Refer people to Customers.
Customers are always with high expectations and if they find if some
requirement is not been provided, they would simply jump to another
alternative and they need not ask anybody for that.For Customers, it has to
work, thats it.So, this is also same for our People, whom we are targetting.

Yes, Linux (the Kernel) is free of cost.Many bundle it in distros and
integrate many items properly to make the newly built distro work. Some give
it for free and other charge a small sum for the distro. There is nothing
wrong in this.Developers spend a lot of time in developing it and in return
if they dont get anything, its like "whats there me working on it?". But
before you charge, you should be confident that your product is worth
charging.Now, why FOSS and OSS ?. Why cant people address just as OSS ?. The
term "Free" in the GPL License does not mean that it is "Free of Cost". If
you want everything for free of cost in this world, then nothing can
be.Anywayz, i wanted to address this becoz people are misleaded.

When we distribute CDs for creating awareness and say Linux Distribution is
an alternate to Windows Operating System, we should also think whether it
would suit their already going on day-to-day activities.There are many
issues with Linux distros like Webcam support,audio and video conferencing.
These, have developed a lot and now we can tell we have a viable solution,
but that solution to work we need to get them integrated
well.Butunfortunately, there are also many restrictions that those
software put. For
example, you cannot bundle Skype along with your distribution. So, telling a
noob user to install (eventhough we have tools), this being a basic need, he
would ask -" why should i,will you not provide me when i install your OS? ".
Even for mp3,dvd supports and other codecs, it is the same.Even if i give
Ubuntu, we dont have these formats included and the first impression once
the distribution is installed is,"i cannot play my mp3s".

There are still things to be enhanced in the Desktop usage side with Linux,
and i think we as LUG have to take care on how we can improve it and there
by create awareness.Becoz, once we propose or tell-> "please use this",
People will come up with many issues and am sure we do know those issues
already.We should have a team to address those issues and resolve. We cannot
give Distros as such and then forget it.

I think all these points should be considered during awareness
programs/campaigns.The main obstacle of people not using Linux in their
desktops, as i see, is the lack of Yahoo/MSN webcam support. Many parents do
Video Chat every week with their son/daughter abroad.How are we going to
tackle issues like these?. We need to discuss on several issues that we
would face.

Basically, i have the habit of categorizing Users/People into different
categories,like,
1) Normal Desktop Users (No Internet, just entertainment, this can also
include Media Center)
2) Normal Desktop Users with Internet Support (which may/not include
Video/Audio Conferencing)
3) Developers/Programmers (non MS developers, like Java/Python etc.,)
4) Gamers (may/not include 2nd type)
5) Combination of 1 + 2+ 3 + 4

I suggest User to try out Linux based on these categories.As far as today,
only for 3rd type of Users,i have been comfortable to suggest.For other
types, i was not able to convince a normal user(who has not been exposed to
Linux at all) to use Linux, there were many issues which were not
answerable.I dont know why, but we feel its easy but if you look at a normal
user and sit with him for 5 mins, you would have atleast 10 issues.

What i feel is, we have few areas to cover up.For example, we have to expose
people to Skype and what one can do with Skype, then Gaim (Gaim 2.0 has
yahoo webcam support), then aMSN (MSN webcam support), linux supported
hardware devices etc.,These have to reach people somehow, whether it is
through campaign or internet or advertisements or writing books or anything.

I feel we need to be ready before we start our awareness programmes.

Just my thoughts....

-- 
Regards,
C.C.Chakkaradeep,
Novatium Solutions Limited,Chennai.
http://www.novatium.com
http://www.yoper.com
http://wiki.freespire.org/index.php/Freespire_Community_Board_Home

Hi,

On 7/7/06, Chakkaradeep C C <chaks.yoper@gmail.com> wrote:
> Basically, i have the habit of categorizing Users/People into different
> categories,like,
> 1) Normal Desktop Users (No Internet, just entertainment, this can also
> include Media Center)
> 2) Normal Desktop Users with Internet Support (which may/not include
> Video/Audio Conferencing)
> 3) Developers/Programmers (non MS developers, like Java/Python y
> 4) Gamers (may/not include 2nd type)
> 5) Combination of 1 + 2+ 3 + 4

Don't do that.

Actually I would say all users are of type 5. A user based in category
1 might not be a developer, but he would like it if his OS was
developer-friendly. Telling him that his OS is just for normal-desktop
use and is not supposed to be a development based desktop will only
turn him off. He might never become a developer but he will be happy
knowing that his OS can also be a developer OS.

My point is, all these custom distro's are good for solving one
problem and one problem only. These sort of problems are usually that
of the GEEKy-type (Ex: I need Media Center s/w on my PIII, I use a
MythTV-Knoppix based distro), not the casual user.

Unless there is major development upstream to address the common
user's issues I dont think we can do much but help out with what we
have now.

just my 0.02$

-Toufeeq

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Fri Jul  7 21:59:43 2006

Date: Fri Jul  7 21:59:52 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Linux and Users

Message-ID: <9a9bfc170607070929q6c26a42fp3b0eb435d4070cf1@mail.gmail.com>

> Actually I would say all users are of type 5. A user based in category
> 1 might not be a developer, but he would like it if his OS was
> developer-friendly. Telling him that his OS is just for normal-desktop
> use and is not supposed to be a development based desktop will only
> turn him off. He might never become a developer but he will be happy
> knowing that his OS can also be a developer OS.

No.. I won't be happy. One of the reasons why I am happier with my
Debian than Windows is that it is able to provide for my system what I
as R.Ramkumar needs, not everything that I as a Mr. Generic User will
probably need. The rest is derogatorily looked down upon the former as
bloat :)

That apart, I think this is an issue which strikes at the heart of
what is the philosophy of the FOSS world, versus other proprietary
vendors. Due to the immense flexibility and freedom, it is but natural
for alternatives to be more specific and focussed. That's why we have
distros customized right for from routers to laptops, from the lay
user to the sophisticated geek.

So, how to make the common man happy? Without troubling him too much,
ask him a single question about what his needs are, and pull out
something out of the hat just perfect for him. When done just to the
right extent, I believe he/she would be happy with the the richness of
the FOSS world.

Adding two more cents to this thread :)

it moves on...

On Fri, 2006-07-07 at 17:20 +0530, Ramanraj K wrote:
> Shrinivasan T wrote:
> 
> > In suse 10, I got a tool called KBittorrent.
> > Is any direct connection to net is needed for Bittorrent?
> >
> > How to make it work?
> 
> BitTorrent is used to download files from the internet using peer to 
> peer sharing, and it helps to reduce load on busy ftp servers and 
> possibly faster downloads from a source close to you.
> 
>  From the file menu of kbittorrent, select "paste bittorrent url", and 
> enter the url of the file you want to download.
> 
> For example, if you want to download the latest FreeBSD 6.1 release 
> iso's, get the url from: http://torrents.freebsd.org:8080/
> 
> On Ubuntu, bittorrent may be invoked from mozilla or firefox. Using 
> synaptic or other package managers, install bittorrent.Open mozilla or 
> firefox.  Point the browser to a bittorrent seed. Click on the file you 
> want to download, and select "open with default application 
> /usr/bin/btdownloadgui " and do the rest.  man btdownloadgui for more info.
> 
> If download is interrupted, you could continue it later and manage it 
> well. BitTorrent generally downloads the iso's etc into directories 
> along with md5 checksums if any.  If you are using k3b to burn the iso 
> to a cd, the integrity of the download is checked automatically.   HTH.
> __
> 
> _______________________________________________
> To unsubscribe, email ilugc-request@ae.iitm.ac.in with 
> "unsubscribe <password> <address>"
> in the subject or body of the message.  
> http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/mailman/listinfo/ilugc

Hello Shakthi:          Attn.: parthan, kenneth, sujith, bharathi, raman

As you are aware, one of the activities of NRCFOSS is to promote FOSS
elective for B.E.(CSE), B.Tech.(IT) and MCA students. Towards this we have
designed two elective papers -- one on the basics and other on Enterprise
applications. Jaya Engg final year students from CSE and IT opted for the
elective during the last summer and Kumaran told me that all of them have
cleared. During the current semester, they want to offer it to MCA -- in
fact both the electives. Their M.Sc students are also interested. We should
appreciate the efforts by Kumaran, Janarthanan and their colleagues (and the
management and students).

Raman and Bharathi had addressed about 40-50 lecturers from different
colleges during the training program we conducted for Elective during last
month. Many of them are keen to conduct LDDs / seminars in their colleges.
We are also trying to set up FOSS labs in all the 50 colleges under our
program (some like Jaya, RMK, Kongu, Sona, Thyagaraja, etc., already have
fully functional FOSS labs).

In my discussions with Raman and Bharathi, we had found merit in one day
training of the students and enabling them to conduct the LDD later
(basically the Arunai experience). I would suggest that you please add
something for students who are not from core computer branches, esp.
Mechanical and ECE. At least one stall could contain demo / exposition on
QCad, Calculix, Scilab, etc. Senthil Anand and Sujith from our group have
done some work on it. Some of  you could come over here on a mutually
convenient day and we can fix up a set. Or else, Parthan (who is already in
with us) can take the lead in this guided by Kenneth.

We can work out a basic structure training and LDD / workshop / half-a-day
seminar. I would suggest that we focus more on the potential use of FOSS and
the various application areas, the opportunity for collaborative development
(and, forgive me, less on the history and philosophy). We could think of a
joint msg to the colleges that ILUG-C and NRCFOSS / AU-KBC are joining to
HELP THE COLLEGES TO ORGANIZE the LDD / seminar. If feasible, I can discuss
with Prof Krishanan (our Director) to transmit the msg thru our Teachers
Mailing group and also put in NRCFOSS portal.

I could then implore the colleges to (a) conduct at least one LDD / lecture
related to FOSS during July-Aug-Sep ; (b) the colleges which have LUG shoud
organize a lecture for the benefit of nearby schools on the Software Freedom
Day ; (c) all the colleges should have a local LUG -- inaugurated on the
LDD/Seminar or on SF Day.

Raman and I had discussed about zone-wise LUGs with apex members interacting
with ILUG-C. This is not to restrict membership, but to co-ordinate and
organize local events more effectively.

Thanks and best wishes, Srinivasan.

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Fri Jul  7 23:14:55 2006
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sat Jul  8 11:45:02 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Linux and Users
In-Reply-To: <E4C7F332-3138-4828-887A-F185F81651B6@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <20060708061455.36432.qmail@web50204.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi all,

--- Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
> reverse engineering?

Yes, if the "protocol" of message passing is in the
public domain.

Most of the vendors form an implementor's forum, where
they prepare a closed/open standard for
interfaces/protocols. USB-IF is an open standard:
http://www.usb.org. All the IETF RFCs are open
standards.

How each vendor implements the standard could be
different and is proprietary. As long as they adhere
to the standard, their product should be compliant and
they can market it to customers. So, you can use Logic
Analysers, snoopers to capture the packets and analyze
what is being transmitted, by comparing the outputs
*with* the open standard protocol.

But, some forums are closed, so you will never know
what protocols are used. Secure Digital, for example.
You will need to pay heavy licensing fees, which
individuals cannot afford to pay. Only companies can
afford such pricing.

http://www.sdcard.org/licensing/hala.html

http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SD_Card

http://lists.infradead.org/pipermail/linux-mtd/2003-July/008166.html

Yet, SD is supported in the Linux kernel, thanks to
feedback from developers in the community.

These days, lot of R&D companies use GNU/Linux, have
support for it, and contribute to it. Its just that
few players are yet to comply.

Regards,

SK

--
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

From raamanp at yahoo.co.in  Sat Jul  8 07:29:18 2006
From: raamanp at yahoo.co.in (Raman.P)

Sorry for little long post on this subject.

A fundamental points that the OP has raised some thing like this

What is the use of propagating linux if I cannot get my webcam
working?
Linux is not fit to be propagated at present, address all issues then
talk about it. Till then will you all shut your mouth?


Last year in India 5 million PCs were sold. But how many webcam? 1
million?

Computer software has diverse use. In a shop, in a home, in school,
in a office, in research and so on. The needs vary.

Yes linux has problems. But be honest, and tell me can't we use
present day distributions in atleast 80-90 percent of places where
computers are used? e.g
a. A office dealing with trivial typing and spread sheet.
b. In schools to teach children
c. In shops and other places of commerce.
d. In government offices

Well the above four itself will account for more than 80% of computer
usage as on date.

Is not linux fit in all these places?. 
If yes how many of these places use linux?

I am sure every body will agree that the usage is nearly 0 %.
What is wrong in creating awarness of FOSS atleast in these areas?
Why don't we look at the possible places where FOSS can already
satisfy the need.

Few months back I studied an NGO, who are working on Rural Health.
They don't need webcam, digital camera,TV tuner card, skype and ....
They just want to type, keep accounts and take printout.
Don't you think FOSS is fit for them?

Basically, OP, looks the world through his experience and feels linux
is not fit. Similarly I see from my experience, that Linux as of
today is fit for NOT LESS than 90% of the places where computer is
used for something.

There are some basic doubts raised about the awarness campaign,
whether it will serve any purpose etc.

My feeling, is let us do something, than simply fear about failures.
Think positively, act with confidence. True there is good chance of
failure, but what is the loss. After all the participant may loose

a.Few hours/days in participation. 
   But it is voluntary. Nobody is forced to participate. Only willing
   people donate time. This should be considered a donation with  
   asking for return.

b.May be some physical discomfort
   Only people who think they can endure and are willing to 
participate.

installation of translation software

downloading of .po files for translation

typing in tamil

translating them either through local gui or over a web interface

submitting the translations for approval

we plan to translate moodle and django - depending on how many people

> Do linux users really hate Java?

I am a Linux user for over 6 years now. And Java is what I work on to
make my living :-). In fact, a lot of people around me work on Java,
on Linux.

You really can't combine these two. If you look at most of the latest
J2EE servers (such as websphere/Oracle WebAppServer), they are
sometimes tailor made to run on Linux (particularly after pThread
fixes). Eclipse (a Java based IDE for almost any prog. lang), is
bundled along with RedHat Linux (and many others).

Do Java developers hate Linux? If the answer is NO, and if they also
work on Linux, they also become a part of Linux users :-P

Raman.P wrote:
> Sorry for little long post on this subject.
> 
> A fundamental points that the OP has raised some thing like this
> 
> What is the use of propagating linux if I cannot get my webcam
> working?
> Linux is not fit to be propagated at present, address all issues then
> talk about it. Till then will you all shut your mouth?
> 

I am afraid that is not the right interpretation of the OP's claim. I
suppose he merely meant that the lack of drivers for certain hardwares
(the web cam as he says and a lot of wi-fi cards I hear) might irk the
common computer user. He probably termed it badly after a long days work
:-) it happens to all of us doesn't it. And yes I agree with you that
the affected group is not a majority at all.

Skype as he mentioned might be proprietary but it is an excellent piece
of software. From Linux's point of view, it would help that more that
softwares creep in (perhaps not from an open source point of view).

On a related note, I was talking to parthan about promoting Linux in
colleges and schools. I was of the opinion that when promoting Linux,
care should be taken so that they adopt Linux along with support (say
something like RHEL). Along the way they may face problems and might
drop off. But if they do have some kind of paid support, they always
have someone to rant to :D.

Parthan on the other hand was of the opinion that Linux will not be
adopted if it is not free (as in beer) since the users who use pirated
versions of software will still not be willing to pay. The cost of an
Operating System with paid support is rather small when compared to the
entire price paid for the hardware along with its support. ``Free
Support'' will make them look forward for more freebies. The concept for
paying for support needs to be imbibed.

I think this lack of a ``commercial'' tinge to Open Source development
is what the OP was initially driving to. I understand that some people
are more comfortable with FLOSS (as I am repeatedly pointed out). My
question is why is it that people repeatedly say ``Use FLOSS not OSS''?
Is it any different in the open spirit if I was to pay for a piece of
software and thereby gain access to its code as against getting the code
with no monetary transactions?

Regards,
- --
Prashanth Mohan
http://prashblog.be

Prashanth Mohan wrote:
  > On a related note, I was talking to parthan about promoting Linux in
> colleges and schools. I was of the opinion that when promoting Linux,
> care should be taken so that they adopt Linux along with support (say
> something like RHEL). Along the way they may face problems and might
> drop off. But if they do have some kind of paid support, they always
> have someone to rant to :D.
> 
> Parthan on the other hand was of the opinion that Linux will not be
> adopted if it is not free (as in beer) since the users who use pirated
> versions of software will still not be willing to pay. The cost of an
> Operating System with paid support is rather small when compared to the
> entire price paid for the hardware along with its support. ``Free
> Support'' will make them look forward for more freebies. The concept for
> paying for support needs to be imbibed.

I am very sorry that Prashanth didn't post the context in which my 
comment was made, as well as the other faces of the argument. That makes 
the above quoted commented of mine to be short-in-focus. We were 
actually arguing how the activities of LUG should be focused and what 
shall be the motive of it. As he said, he was trying to justify adding a 
price tagged model or may be said as commercial model and not as 'free' 
model.

IMO, the activity of the Linux community such as ilugc can be focused on 
three different kind of people,

1. Linux Users ( i.e. within the community)
2. Students and teachers
3. Common men who are in need of an economic solution.

Considering these 3 types of people, the approach of LUG towards each 
type is very different.

Considering the academic community, consisting of students and teachers, 
who are atleast computer literates to some extent, if not Open Source 
literates. And, the fact is also that they have been using proprietary 
software for a long time. Our aim should be to make them FOSS aware and 
with a little of motivation and effort we can achieve this. This is 
what, ilugc has been doing through LDDs and seminars held in various 
colleges/schools and plan to carry the same further in the future. 
Considering the schools,  who may not be as wealthy as colleges, is it a 
viable option for them to buy RHEL ? Do they really need things like 
RHEL, when they are just beginning to get into OSS. I do not commit to 
Prash's argument that 'along the way, problems might turn them off/drop 
them off". We, in ilugc, not only strive to create linux/OSS awareness 
but also ready to help academic people become OSS literates. We showed 
this with our arunai college experience, where ilugc was able to train a 
group of volunteers who were able to run the LDD very much upon 
themselves, backed by the ilugc. And for the kind information, we didn't 
put up any banner like 'free CDs' will be distributed and perhaps din't 
give any. Still there was a huge crowd turn up that day. Hence, we 
believe that the term 'Free' as in 'Free beer' is not mandatory w.r.t. 
academic community.

Considering the common men, who are need of support of computers but 
can't afford for costly solutions like RHEL support. These people aren't 
really computer savvy but the seek the help of computers to make their 
work simple. For these people, 'Free' as in 'Free beer' does matter a 
lot. In this way, the Open Source can help them a lot. It is also true 
that, the requirements of these people can be solved with 'free as in 
free beer' softwares available in open source world today. If not, a 
solution can be developed with an economically viable price tag for them 
in OSS.

People don't understand when you speak them the benefits of OSS, but 
surely when you show them. Thats what we do, by holding LDDs. Indeed, 
ilugc wishes and plans to reach more people in the academic community as 
well as the common men who are in need of OSS's help :)

With Regards

Parthan ('technofreak')
------------------------------
Research Assistant @ NRC-FOSS and Python\PHP Developer
A Proud Tuxian and an Ubuntero

Friends.

After finishing yesterdays meet, me(Shrini) and buvan went to ELCOT Office.

Interesting matters held there.

Buvan installed Ubuntu in Mr.UmaSankar's Laptop.
Before, it had Redhat and XP. He had some documents at Redhat.
So, While buvan asked him to remove XP, He accepted with no thinking.

He installed it nicely.

Meanwhile, I went to make tamil unicode typing at Openoffice.

It is simple in Opensuse KDE.
In persenal settings->Region&accebility->Keyboard Layout
It is there to add tamil unicode.

Then put the ~ key to switch the layout.
Thats it. Well done, I hoped.

But there is some real problem in unicode tamil keyboard layout.
It is not purely 100% Remington Typewriter layout.
Sakthi has unicode layout in his site.
I phoned him and gave the people there.

They found some problem in this layout.
As they have 10+ experience in Remington layout,
They feel very tough to adapt this unicode layout.

And the font "Lohit tamil" give some space problems.
It adds ore extra spaces while typing. So alignment is tough.

The requirement is
1. A tamil unicode keyboard layout 100% compitable with remington layout.
2. It should not gice any extra spaces.

Any one has taml typing experience in linux?
How do u solve this?
please mail me,list or hi ur experiences.

Then, He showed the conference hall for GLV. It is nice.

Buvan installed Ubuntu. He likes its automounting options.
It played his DVD movie automatically.
It asked to open the folder when he inserted his thumb drive.

At last, he made his drive to drop me at villivakkam, my place, with some staff.

Thus, He is more interested in FOSS.
With his efforts, Tamilnadu may become FOSS Station.

Thank you all.

dear,
T.Shrinivasan.

My thoughts below:

First thing you should choose is the laptop screen
size that you want. The bigger the screen, greater is
the battery size, and greater the weight. Depending on
how fit you are, you might choose between light-weight
or heavy laptops.

> Intel Centrino, or
> AMD64 (Turion)? Which one is best supported by
> Linux? (I did hear rumors that AMD64 causes problems
> on most distros)

Never tried AMD64, but, you can browse here:

http://www.linux-laptop.net/

You can also google for HOWTOs or tutorials by people
who have installed x distribution on y laptop, or
simply GNU/Linux on y laptop.

> Which distro? SUSE, Ubuntu, Mandriva or Fedora? 

Choice of distro is a personal preference. I'd
recommend any recent distro.

> And
> where to get that in Chennai?

Note :
1. Threads about distros and things like favourite softwares, favourite 
programming languages are known to start 'Flame Wars'
2. Before asking any question, try to do some google, try something 
based on the results and then post when you find no clue out.
3. Donot copy the entire contents of logs and other outputs here. Rather 
paste them to pastebin.de and just give the links in your mail.
4. Try to have a easily understandable and relevant title for your 
posts, which will help us.

Hope, someone will give you the common mailing list guidelines which 
will help you know better. Otherwise, learning through experience is 
always there ;)

Agreed., but only partially. If you look at majority of the software

in-house projects (very much specific to business and has business
secrets built into them).

to marketing by companies like IBM, BEA, ...), people have implemented
some very good platforms for enterprise level architectures. I have of
course coded on C/C++, PHP, CGI PERL, VB, VC++, COBOL and Java. I am
not here to say that, something is impossible to do in C++ and is
possible on Java, but it is just the easiness of implementation that
is available on Java for ENTERPRISE APPLICATION projects, as per
CURRENT standards. There is no doubt that C/C++ is always superior in
terms of speed, but implementation and development/maintenance  costs
are of course higher.

> I am a new-recruit programmer at American Int'l Group (AIG), and will be buying a laptop soon. But I'm too much confused:
> Which architecture to choose? Intel Centrino, or AMD64 (Turion)? Which one is best supported by Linux? (I did hear rumors that AMD64 causes problems on most distros)

The Centrino vs Turion is a good debate and here are my thoughts..

The centrino is good if you want great performance-per-watt, meaning
you will get more done for less power which inturn means your battery
life will be more per charge. The turion is great if you are
interested in a desktop-replacement. If you are going to be travelling
a bit, go for the centrino, if performance and games are important
then turion. Both are well supported under Linux.

A point to consider, Intel's Core Duo 2 will be launched later this
month and laptops based on that should arrive soon after. The new
turion's are also impressive. If you dont mind waiting , I suggest you
wait till Nov-Dec and see how good they are.

I bought a laptop last week, the Dell XPS m1210, it's centrino based
and a compact one yet packs a lot of power. I wrote up a small preview
of it too: http://toufeeq.blogspot.com/2006/06/dell-xps-m1210.html

> Which distro? SUSE, Ubuntu, Mandriva or Fedora? And where to get that in Chennai?
> I shall be using my Tux machine for development in J2EE, OpenLaszlo & Perl, with Apache running around. Yeah, and also for office, multimedia and the internet.

Since this is your first foray into Linux, stick to the road. Choose
either Ubuntu 6.06, Fedora Core 5 or Open SUSE 10.

have fun,

From rajanvn at gmail.com  Sun Jul  9 22:30:28 2006
From: rajanvn at gmail.com (Natarajan V)
Date: Sun Jul  9 22:30:35 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Enterprise (business) architectures on Linux
Message-ID: <e977d4310607091000o2aa92488i56bbc8cca01f19a4@mail.gmail.com>

Hi all,

For quite some time now, I have been wondering if there are any
platforms/architectures available for enterprise business applications
on a Linux platform? (if none available, lets start one :-) )

I will try to explain what kind of enterprise application I am talking about.

A business (lets say a bank) wants to build its software (may be from
scratch). It wants its software to be user friendly, scalable reliable
and future proof.

It should be possible to throw in some extra hardware to meet an
increase in usage, without modifying the software. It must also be
possible to add in new interfaces or business modules or change the
existing applications at will. Also the GUIs will be developed by
professional designers and ergonomics experts while the business
logic's will be done by geeks.

Certainly, we cannot put a Apache WS/PHP (alone) or LAMP for this
situation. Here in the corporate world, the database is HUGE. The
number of applications(modules) are also huge. Just as Mr. Umashankar
explained, in his application, the student councilors are interested
in the details of the students, while the Finance dept is interested
in the money that they have collected. The admin is more interested in
the courses/students statistics. We will be building separate
modules/applications for these. Some of these WILL NOT be web based,
while some WILL BE web based. Also, there are parts which are
accessible only to the employees while some are accessible to the
students.

Those who have worked with a Web Based application, would be familiar
with the number of fields that are available per screen and the number
of reports that are generated. A Discussion forum  application is
"NOT" an example for the kind of sophistication that I am quoting
here.

For this kind of applications, a few things are mandatory:
1. MVC 2 architecture
      The display logic should be independent of the business
implementation. a PHP code that writes out HTML output should not be
accessing the database directly.

2. Separation of Business Logic as a separate entity, which can be
accessed either though a desktop application or through a web
application or a B2B application. (may be through CORBA, for example).

3. A transaction manager which can do the work of Containers in a J2EE
environment or CICS in a IBM Main frame environment. (I don't want two
programs to access the same database. Don't even give an opportunity
even for two versions of the same program to access the same tables).

4. Message queuing.

5. Interface to other applications, across platforms and sometimes
across corporates (two companies have joined hands and so want their
softwares also to join hands).

6. Load balancing, clustering, distributed computing etc... as per
requirement or may be added in future.

The above list is NOT exhaustive, but these are essential.

The above features are available in a J2EE environment as well as in
M$ environments (though not as robust as in J2EE). Even IBM Z/OS by
means of CICS is able to handle such situations to a great extent.

I have seen people using Linux clustering and other frameworks as the
underlying platform, while using J2EE for their business
implementation. J2EE servers (such as WebSphere, WebLogic, Open Source
JBOSS), take care of the configuration issues (such as load balancing,
etc.,) and they also provide a separation between presentation and
business (Struts and EJB for example - slightly outdated)

Now to my actual question:
----------------------------------
Are there any "neatly packaged" platforms available in Linux which can
handle the above said situations?

-----------------------------------

I can very well use PHP.MVC for the presentation(v1 just released),
write a separate C/C++ program which has a CORBA interface for the
business logic, and connect them together. If some one wants to build
a desktop front end for the business, they can do so using CORBA. But
the process is too cumbersome. It is just not neatly packaged. I am
also not able to find any transaction managers for Linux from Google.
May be I did not use the correct key words.

----------------------
I am not expecting any out of the box answers to the question. But any
constructive discussion is welcome. If you want me to describe any of
the points, please do not hesitate to shoot your questions :-).

PS: My answers will be a little delayed due to  mail accessibility.


with regards,
Natarajan.

From nallu.ignacius at gmail.com  Mon Jul 10 08:16:07 2006
From: nallu.ignacius at gmail.com (nallu ignacius)
Date: Mon Jul 10 08:16:16 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Enterprise (business) architectures on Linux
In-Reply-To: <e977d4310607091000o2aa92488i56bbc8cca01f19a4@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e977d4310607091000o2aa92488i56bbc8cca01f19a4@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a1a229120607091946p711fa20apd951b095799a90fc@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Natrajan,

I have worked in one such project.
It is a J2EE architecture based application.


On 7/9/06, Natarajan V <rajanvn@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> Hi all,
>
> For quite some time now, I have been wondering if there are any
> platforms/architectures available for enterprise business applications
> on a Linux platform? (if none available, lets start one :-) )
>
> I will try to explain what kind of enterprise application I am talking
> about.
>
> A business (lets say a bank) wants to build its software (may be from
> scratch). It wants its software to be user friendly, scalable reliable
> and future proof.
>
> It should be possible to throw in some extra hardware to meet an
> increase in usage, without modifying the software. It must also be
> possible to add in new interfaces or business modules or change the
> existing applications at will. Also the GUIs will be developed by
> professional designers and ergonomics experts while the business
> logic's will be done by geeks.
>
> Certainly, we cannot put a Apache WS/PHP (alone) or LAMP for this
> situation. Here in the corporate world, the database is HUGE. The
> number of applications(modules) are also huge. Just as Mr. Umashankar
> explained, in his application, the student councilors are interested
> in the details of the students, while the Finance dept is interested
> in the money that they have collected. The admin is more interested in
> the courses/students statistics. We will be building separate
> modules/applications for these. Some of these WILL NOT be web based,
> while some WILL BE web based. Also, there are parts which are
> accessible only to the employees while some are accessible to the
> students.
>
> Those who have worked with a Web Based application, would be familiar
> with the number of fields that are available per screen and the number
> of reports that are generated. A Discussion forum  application is
> "NOT" an example for the kind of sophistication that I am quoting
> here.
>
> For this kind of applications, a few things are mandatory:
> 1. MVC 2 architecture
>       The display logic should be independent of the business
> implementation. a PHP code that writes out HTML output should not be
> accessing the database directly.
>
> 2. Separation of Business Logic as a separate entity, which can be
> accessed either though a desktop application or through a web
> application or a B2B application. (may be through CORBA, for example).
>
> 3. A transaction manager which can do the work of Containers in a J2EE
> environment or CICS in a IBM Main frame environment. (I don't want two
> programs to access the same database. Don't even give an opportunity
> even for two versions of the same program to access the same tables).
>
> 4. Message queuing.
>
> 5. Interface to other applications, across platforms and sometimes
> across corporates (two companies have joined hands and so want their
> softwares also to join hands).
>
> 6. Load balancing, clustering, distributed computing etc... as per
> requirement or may be added in future.
>
> The above list is NOT exhaustive, but these are essential.
>
> The above features are available in a J2EE environment as well as in
> M$ environments (though not as robust as in J2EE). Even IBM Z/OS by
> means of CICS is able to handle such situations to a great extent.
>
> I have seen people using Linux clustering and other frameworks as the
> underlying platform, while using J2EE for their business
> implementation. J2EE servers (such as WebSphere, WebLogic, Open Source
> JBOSS), take care of the configuration issues (such as load balancing,
> etc.,) and they also provide a separation between presentation and
> business (Struts and EJB for example - slightly outdated)
>
> Now to my actual question:
> ----------------------------------
> Are there any "neatly packaged" platforms available in Linux which can
> handle the above said situations?
>
> -----------------------------------
>


I can very well use PHP.MVC for the presentation(v1 just released),
> write a separate C/C++ program which has a CORBA interface for the
> business logic, and connect them together. If some one wants to build
> a desktop front end for the business, they can do so using CORBA. But
> the process is too cumbersome. It is just not neatly packaged. I am
> also not able to find any transaction managers for Linux from Google.
> May be I did not use the correct key words.


The adoption of J2EE architecture can be like this

Client [HTML/CSS compliant browser] ==>
Web tier [PHP running on a Apache server acting as Business delegate] ==>
Axis Web service ==>
Business Tier [ EJBs deployed in a JBoss App Server] ==> Hibernate for OR
mapping ==>
Information Tier [MySQL with InnoDB or Postgres]

The advantage is that you can open up your web services through Axis. Web
services compliant applications can access the needed web service based on
proper authentication.


regards,
Ignacius

You can try this http://www.spikesource.com/products/corestack.html if you
want to setup the environment without much trouble[but I haven't tried
this].

----------------------
> I am not expecting any out of the box answers to the question. But any
> constructive discussion is welcome. If you want me to describe any of
> the points, please do not hesitate to shoot your questions :-).
>
> PS: My answers will be a little delayed due to  mail accessibility.
>
>
> with regards,
> Natarajan.

> Is there any way to install it from the console itself?

The one they ship is desktop intall CD. It can be used as live &
install CD. When we boot, the gui is loaded and we have "Install"
icon. We can double-click the icon to start the installation, and
yeah, it only has gui mode of installation.

To install it from console, I guess you should download the "Alternate
install CD" from www.u.c/download.

From bhuvan at ubuntu.com  Mon Jul 10 13:09:00 2006

Let me summarize the minutes of meeting.

Around 15 of members met in the venue. As it took sometime for
Mr.Umashankar to arrive we discussed about organising the walk. There
has been couple of light comments about the way we co-ordinate this
event. We have plans to invite couple of colleges to participate.
Next, Bhuvan distributed the Ubuntu Tshirts to couple of members.

Next, a member (please update his name) explained about the purpose of
GPLV3. He stated couple of differences betweeen it and its
counterpart. We also discussed about its impact in GNU/Linux
licensing.

Meanwhile, Mr.Umashankar have arrived. Bharathi formally introduced
him to the group and left the stage for him. Mr.Umashankar explained
why he is here and what he expects. He spoke for around 2hrs (?) and
cleared indicated what he expects from the community.

Summary:

1) ELCOT is setting up a call-center to support the staffs of all
Govt. departments. The call center agents will provide support to
them. In case they cant, they will escalate it to the ILUGC volunteer
who may be on call. If he is available, he can attend. If he is not
available, he can send a message so it will be escalated to next
volunteer in queue. The volunteers would be paid for every
successful/unsuccessful call they attend. They are in the process to
building an website specifically for this purpose.
2) ELCOT is planning to setup software development R&D center. It is
expected to be opened during jan 2007 in chennai. He need volunteers
to recruit and train the staffs. The softwares developed by this team
would be used by many Govt. departments and it will be released under
an open source license.
3) He need volunteers across all district headquarters to support the
staffs of the Govt. departments when they face issues.

On hand he had an issue with setting Tamil unicode font for linux. He
needed someone from our group to setup. Shrinivasan volunteered to do
that. Next, he was so happy using opensuse. Couple of Ubuntu fans in
the group suggested him to try as it is very cool. He gladly accepted
it and needed someone from our group to install and configure. Bhuvan
volunteered to do that.

In addition, he also accepted to host monthly/weekly ILUGC meeting at
his premise. He also confirmed to provide coffee and tiffin to all
participants! (As soon as he returned to office it was the first order
he passed)

Finally, Raman acknowledged his requirements and confirmed that ILUGC
would devise a plan to address those needs. He also hinted about the
walk we are planning and we may seek his assistance!

Thats all i can recollect. Please feel free to correct/add more points
if i have missed any. Thank you!
-- 
Regards,
Bhuvaneswaran
www.symonds.net/~bhuvan/
GPG: 0x7A13E5B0

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Mon Jul 10 12:10:09 2006
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Tue Jul 11 00:40:16 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] graphics card problem.
In-Reply-To: <1152553650.5387.26.camel@localhost.localdomain>
Message-ID: <20060710191009.5722.qmail@web50207.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi Deepan and others,

--- Deepan Chakravarthy <codeshepherd@gmail.com>
wrote:
> When i compile   i915-20060403-linux.i386 i get the
> error cannot file
> the kernel config file. I had install the
> kernel-devel package. 

Check if you have a .config file in your kernel source
directory, probably /usr/src/2.6.17-1.2145_FC5smp/.
Its a hidden file so use "ls -a".

> The DRI drivers can not be installed without the
> latest kernel modules.

1. You need to have a .config file in the sources
directory. You can do "make oldconfig" to create the
.config file or do "make menuconfig" and then exit,
save to save the current configuration to a .config
file in the kernel sources directory.

2. The kernel sources should have been compiled, with
the modules installed at /lib/modules.

> Makefile:173: *** Cannot find a kernel config file. 
> Stop.
 
Lack of .config file.

When you are compiling a driver module, you are
compiling and linking against kernel objects (which
should exist). 

Its like compiling a user-application against glibc
headers.

Regards,

SK

Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Tue Jul 11 14:00:51 2006
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Tue Jul 11 14:01:01 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] code formatting in emacs?
In-Reply-To: <dc538c3f0607110125t41e28042pb89fbf60d32c9e93@mail.gmail.com>
References: <dc538c3f0607110125t41e28042pb89fbf60d32c9e93@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <44B361BB.5050409@frodo.hserus.net>

balachandar muruganantham wrote:
> Hi,
> 
> i am using emacs in fedora core 3.
> 
> how do i do code formatting in a existing php script? like setting
> indentation automatically?
> 

M-x php-mode

more detailed - stick this in your .emacs

;
; Bug in 'css-mode when "required"
;
;(require 'css-mode)
(autoload 'css-mode "css-mode")
(add-to-list 'auto-mode-alist '("\\.css\\'" . css-mode))
(add-hook 'css-mode-hook 'turn-on-font-lock)

(require 'php-mode)
(autoload 'php-mode "php-mode" "PHP editing mode" t)

;; normally you'd have these uncommented, but we are
;; going to treat them as HTML/PHP files.
;(add-to-list 'auto-mode-alist '("\\.php\\'" . php-mode))
;(add-to-list 'auto-mode-alist '("\\.inc\\'" . php-mode))
(add-hook 'php-mode-user-hook 'turn-on-font-lock)

(require 'javascript-mode)
(autoload 'javascript-mode "javascript-mode" "Javascript Editing Mode" t)
(add-to-list 'auto-mode-alist '("\\.js\\'" . javascript-mode))
(add-hook 'javascript-mode-hook 'turn-on-font-lock)

(require 'mmm-mode)
(setq mmm-global-mode 'maybe)
;; set up an mmm group for fancy html editing
(mmm-add-group
  'fancy-html
  '(
    (html-css-attribute
     :submode css-mode
     :face mmm-declaration-submode-face
     :delimiter-mode nil
     :front "style=\""
     :back "\"")
    )
)
;; What files to invoke the new html-mode for?
(add-to-list 'auto-mode-alist '("\\.html?\\'" . html-mode))
(add-to-list 'auto-mode-alist '("\\.php\\'" . html-mode))

;; What features should be turned on in this html-mode?
(add-to-list 'mmm-mode-ext-classes-alist '(html-mode nil html-js))
(add-to-list 'mmm-mode-ext-classes-alist '(html-mode nil html-php))
(add-to-list 'mmm-mode-ext-classes-alist '(html-mode nil embedded-css))
(add-to-list 'mmm-mode-ext-classes-alist '(html-mode nil fancy-html))

;;http://www.emacswiki.org/cgi-bin/wiki/HtmlToc
(defun html-show-toc ()
    "Shows a TOC based on headings tags <H[1-6]>"
    (interactive)
    (if sgml-tags-invisible
        (error "SGML tags are invisible")
      (occur "<h[1-6]>")
      (pop-to-buffer "*Occur*")
      (vc-toggle-read-only)
      (goto-char (point-min))
      (replace-string "<h1>" "")
      (goto-char (point-min))
      (replace-string "<h2>" "  ")
      (goto-char (point-min))
      (replace-string "<h3>" "    ")
      (goto-char (point-min))
      (replace-string "<h4>" "      ")
      (goto-char (point-min))
      (replace-string "<h5>" "        ")
      (goto-char (point-min))
      (replace-string "<h6>" "          ")
      (goto-char (point-min))
      (replace-regexp "</h[1-6]>" "")
      (goto-char (point-min))
      (toggle-read-only 1)))
From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Tue Jul 11 14:04:15 2006
From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (R.Ramkumar)
Date: Tue Jul 11 14:04:27 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] code formatting in emacs?
In-Reply-To: <dc538c3f0607110125t41e28042pb89fbf60d32c9e93@mail.gmail.com>
References: <dc538c3f0607110125t41e28042pb89fbf60d32c9e93@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <9a9bfc170607110134r6180de8fr3e05cc41da973be1@mail.gmail.com>

> how do i do code formatting in a existing php script? like setting
> indentation automatically?

As and when you type the php script, emacs indents it automatically.
If you want to indent an existing script, select the region (maybe the
whole buffer: `C-x h') and use indent-region (bound to C-` in my
setup, i am not sure if this is the default)

it moves on...

From: stylesen at gmail.com (Senthil Kumaran S)

Subject: [Ilugc] code formatting in emacs?
In-Reply-To: <dc538c3f0607110144u14a3905eobe0b2f6ca30a749c@mail.gmail.com>
References: <dc538c3f0607110125t41e28042pb89fbf60d32c9e93@mail.gmail.com>
	<9a9bfc170607110134r6180de8fr3e05cc41da973be1@mail.gmail.com>
	<dc538c3f0607110144u14a3905eobe0b2f6ca30a749c@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <5ef2113c0607110150lebaacect3ea4cefd17491aa7@mail.gmail.com>

> > whole buffer: `C-x h') and use indent-region (bound to C-` in my
>
> i couldnt understand the above line. all i use is default settings. i
> am not using any keybindings.

The above lines is nothing but if you have an existing code in php and
wants to indent that code, then you have to open the file where the
code is and use the keys `C-x h', so that the whole file is marked.
Then use `M-x indent-region' which will indent the whole php file
(most accurately the buffer) which has the php code.

Just had a look at one of the centre's research project (I am not sure if
its world class).
http://au-kbc.org/research_areas/nlp/projects/sengine.html

This page talks about creating a search engine for tamil. Already google is
there and we can do searching using unicode tamil (or any other encoding -
but our google interface should be changed accordingly to show the encoding
correctly ). I find google does this job very effectively.
For example,
You please enter this tamil text ??????????? (just cut and paste) in your
google search and enter.

From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Tue Jul 11 14:28:31 2006
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Tue Jul 11 14:28:43 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Help on gnus config
In-Reply-To: <5ef2113c0607110146w75d17dc3kda4779a3b8deb0f5@mail.gmail.com>
References: <5ef2113c0607110146w75d17dc3kda4779a3b8deb0f5@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <44B36837.1060309@frodo.hserus.net>

Senthil Kumaran S wrote:
> (setq gnus-select-method '(nntp "news.gnus.org"))
> (add-to-list 'gnus-secondary-select-methods '(nnml ""))
> (setq mail-sources '((pop :server "pop.gmail.com"
>                          :user "stylesen@gmail.com"
>                          :password "secret")))

gmail has pop3 + ssl (different port)

it has smtp auth + ssl (again you need to enable ssl + login / passwd 
credentials)

.gnus.el:
(eval-after-load "mail-source" '(require 'pop3)) ;; pop3 with ssl support

(setq smtpmail-debug-info t)
(setq pop3-debug t)

(setq user-full-name "Name")
(setq user-mail-address "mailname@gmail.com")

;;POP mail

(setq mail-sources
       '(;
         (pop :server "pop.gmail.com"
              :port 995
              :user "mailname@gmail.com"
              :connection ssl
              :leave t)))

;; Sending mail
(setq message-send-mail-function 'smtpmail-send-it)
(setq smtpmail-starttls-credentials '(("smtp.gmail.com" 587 nil nil)))
(setq smtpmail-auth-credentials '(("smtp.gmail.com" 587 "mailname@gmail.com"
  nil)))
(setq smtpmail-default-smtp-server "smtp.gmail.com")
(setq smtpmail-smtp-server "smtp.gmail.com")
(setq smtpmail-smtp-service 587)

On Tue, 11 Jul 2006, rahul wrote:

> My target system is powerpc , linux-2.6.11. when i give the lspci in
> my target system , it says "can't find the command".

Normally lspci is in /sbin/ dir. AFAIK, It is not the part of busybox. 
It is from pciutils tools. Copy the lspci command from PPC Toolchain 
to your PPC filesystem.

> gmail has pop3 + ssl (different port)

Vanilla gnus/gnus shipped with Emacs in CVS doesn't come with ssl
support, or atleast didn't some time back (I haven't seen pop3.el from
the CVS HEAD of late). A version of gnus, called T-Gnus has support
for ssl (apart from other pop3 features like uidl). See this page:

http://www.pvv.ntnu.no/~terjeros/wiki/GnusGmail

Claus Gindhart wrote:

>Rahul,
>
>you need to download the pciutils (e.g. 2.1.11) tarball, and cross compile it 
>for PPC.
>
>However, i had to patch the configure script to make it cross-compilable. Here 
>is the patch
>
>---------------------------8-<-----------------------------------------------
>diff -Nurd pciutils-2.1.11.ori/lib/configure pciutils-2.1.11/lib/configure
>--- pciutils-2.1.11.ori/lib/configure   2003-01-04 13:29:23.000000000 +0100
>+++ pciutils-2.1.11/lib/configure       2006-05-29 11:08:00.000000000 +0200
>@@ -12,17 +12,20 @@
> echo_n "Configuring libpci for your system..."
> sharedir=${1:-/usr/share}
> version=${2:-0.0}
>-sys=`uname -s`
>-rel=`uname -r`
>-if [ "$sys" = "AIX" -a -x /usr/bin/oslevel -a -x /usr/sbin/lsattr ]
>-then
>-       rel=`/usr/bin/oslevel`
>-       proc=`/usr/sbin/lsdev -C -c processor -S available -F name | head -1`
>-       cpu=`/usr/sbin/lsattr -F value -l $proc -a type | sed 's/_.*//'`
>-else
>-       cpu=`uname -m | sed 's/^i.86$/i386/;s/^sun4u$/sparc64/'`
>-fi
>-echo " $sys/$cpu $rel"
>+sys=Linux
>+rel=2.6.13
>+cpu=ppc
>+#sys=`uname -s`
>+#rel=`uname -r`
>+#if [ "$sys" = "AIX" -a -x /usr/bin/oslevel -a -x /usr/sbin/lsattr ]
>+#then
>+#      rel=`/usr/bin/oslevel`
>+#      proc=`/usr/sbin/lsdev -C -c processor -S available -F name | head -1`
>+#      cpu=`/usr/sbin/lsattr -F value -l $proc -a type | sed 's/_.*//'`
>+#else
>+#      cpu=`uname -m | sed 's/^i.86$/i386/;s/^sun4u$/sparc64/'`
>+#fi
>+#echo " $sys/$cpu $rel"
> 
> c=config.h
> echo >$c "#define ARCH_`echo $cpu | tr 'a-z' 'A-Z'`"
>---------------------------8-<-----------------------------------------------
>
>For the build, i called
>export CROSS=$(CROSS_COMPILE)
>make HOST=$(ARCH)
>
>However, depending on your environment, it might by slightly different in your 
>case.
>

> > a setq when gnus loads should do... put up ur .gnus in paste.lisp.org

>
> I ve pasted my .gnus.el file here
> http://paste.lisp.org/display/22398

> but it stands still and am unable to do anything after that.

1. I hope there is no problem with the network, and that gmail is
accessible without a proxy.
2. See if the pop3.el which is getting loaded is the one you
downloaded and not the one from gnus... use `M-x find-library pop3' to
see the full path. If it points to the gnus thing, put your source in
some other folder of yours, say, ~/.emacs.d/shadow and insert `(setq
load-path (cons "~/.emacs.d/shadow" load-path))' in ur .emacs.

it moves on...

it would be unfair to blame linux for "new concepts" like package
manager, or symlinks, or X server. for a grandmother will be as
confused with those as Start Menu, Folder, or Run dialog or Control
Panel. not a hobbyist or someone passionate, but every1 who is first
introduced to a comp, with Windows, has to get used to it. it is just
that the terminology is different in linux, and had you started off
your comp life with Linux, you would have found shifting to Windows as
difficult. that's something we got to leave.

hi all,

On 7/11/06, R. Ramkumar <andyetitmoves@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> it would be unfair to blame linux for "new concepts" like package
> manager, or symlinks, or X server. for a grandmother will be as
> confused with those as Start Menu, Folder, or Run dialog or Control
> Panel. not a hobbyist or someone passionate, but every1 who is first
> introduced to a comp, with Windows, has to get used to it. it is just
> that the terminology is different in linux, and had you started off
> your comp life with Linux, you would have found shifting to Windows as
> difficult. that's something we got to leave.


i agree with ramkumar.. i started using computers with windows (From windows
3.1 till XP).. when i thought of shifting to linux, i came across various
difficulties. When i think me as a normal user, i would have decided to not
use linux since i need to learn more new concepts.. But, as a developer, i
decided to learn and adapt and facinated by the GNU, GPL principles. and
eventually skipped Windows..

It took more time for me to shift from windows to Linux. for a novice user,
switching to linux takes some more time. But, I recently heard about my
friends who started using computers with GNU/Linux loaded.. impossible..
they dont like to work in windows.. and can easily differentiate the powers
of linux over windows..

So, the only way to stop comments that Linux is difficult is to "ask the
people who not even touched the computer to start working on linux".. like
grandpa and grandma..

More than me, here there will be many guys who started working on computers
with GNU/Linux.. Ur opinions will be better than me..

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Jul 11 18:18:24 2006
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Tue Jul 11 18:17:56 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Free Software Meeting - France
Message-ID: <1621.61.247.255.57.1152622104.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

Hi,

I have just attended the Free (Libre) Software Meeting held at Nancy, France.

http://www.rmll.info/rub_1?lang=en

This is an annual meeting of free software developers and experts from
across the globe.

I presented seminars on free software usage for patient and healthcare
data privacy and security for the EU member states. We were also able to
showcase some of the software currently under development for the
monitoring of chronic diseases in India.

I was able to meet many of the primary developers of many interesting
F/LOSS software including:
- GDL - GNU Data Language
- R - Another language used for statistical studies
- Octave - An application growing more and more similar to Mathlab
- MedInTux - An excellent healthcare product developed by a very small team
- Zope 3
- TurboGears - A Python application framework
- RoR
- LinBox - Linux directory service
- ObjectWeb - JAVA Middleware
- GoSA2 - A package for managing directory services including LDAP
- TinyERP
- RoseGarden - An audio authoring / composing tool.
- Blender - An excellent tutorial was presented
- NetBSD - one of the primary maintainers was available.
- OpenBSD
- OpenWengo

I was somewhat disappointed with the lacklustre show from India
considering that F/LOSS software is used a lot here. I was only one of two
Indians to participate in any capacity in this conference. The other
Indian and I were team members and we presented some of the seminars
together - he is a physician.

It may be interesting to look at why India doesn't contribute as much to
F/LOSS as might be expected.

Regards,
Prem Kurian Philip
Songbird Technologies

-----BEGIN PGP SIGNED MESSAGE-----
Hash: SHA1

Shrinivasan T wrote:
> Is there anyway to copy those packages from my pc to them?
> In synaptec, i choosed the option not to delete the files after
> downloading.
> where will they be? ccan i use them for other systems?

these files would be in /var/cache/apt/archives

you could manually copy these files to your friends system and try to
install them using dpkg. `dpkg -i <file>'

As for your specific requirement, there is work in progress (the first
line will probably solve your needs but it is a little complex as of now):

http://ubuntu.wordpress.com/2006/07/08/installing-packages-on-computers-with-slow-connections-redux/
http://code.google.com/soc/ubuntu/appinfo.html?csaid=620C62A612446B12
https://wiki.ubuntu.com/OfflineUpdateSpec


- --
Prashanth Mohan

Claus Gindhart wrote:

>Hi Rahul,
>
>Maybe, its better, if you do the modification by hand. This has the advantage, 
>that you know, what happens.
>
>Just, search for the following lines
>--------------8-<----------------------
>sys=`uname -s`
>rel=`uname -r`
>if [ "$sys" = "AIX" -a -x /usr/bin/oslevel -a -x /usr/sbin/lsattr ]
>then
>      rel=`/usr/bin/oslevel`
>      proc=`/usr/sbin/lsdev -C -c processor -S available -F name | head -1`
>      cpu=`/usr/sbin/lsattr -F value -l $proc -a type | sed 's/_.*//'`
>else
>      cpu=`uname -m | sed 's/^i.86$/i386/;s/^sun4u$/sparc64/'`
>fi
>echo " $sys/$cpu $rel"
>--------------8-<----------------------
>
>Comment them out; they can not work, when cross compiling, because they try to 
>detect Kernel version and architecture by using host tools
>
>Then, add the following lines
>
>--------------8-<----------------------
>sys=Linux
>rel=2.6.13 (or whatever Kernel version you have)
>cpu=ppc
>--------------8-<----------------------
>
>
>
>

On 7/12/06, Chakkaradeep C C <chaks.yoper@gmail.com> wrote:
> Is it not possible to put the local location in the sources.list and do apt
> update and then install those packages?

apt does not look at the packages (debs) themselves.  It looks for the
Packages(.gz) index file.  As Kumar suggested, you need to use
dpkg-scanpackages to create it.  There are subtle issues with versioning
etc that you can run into if you are not careful.  dpkg-scanpackages is
really for advanced users (and people who have an affection towards man
pages!)

To the OP:  copying your *.deb files into your friends
/var/cache/apt/archives and then running apt/synaptic should work.  If the
debs are found in the said directory, apt will not attempt to download the
files again.  However, you still need to run the equivalent of "apt-get update"
first.  You don't need to run dpkg-scanpackages if you do it this way.

If you don't want to copy the debs to /var/cache/apt/archives, you can
set the Dir::Cache::Archives config item appropriately.  I think this can
specified on the cmd line for one-off runs, but I've never done it this
way.  I'm interested in knowing if this works for you.

On Debian, /usr/share/doc-base/apt-offline-usage-guide would be a good
read.

- Raja
