--- Aanjhan R <aanjhan@gmail.com> wrote:
> Seems like a lot of people are talking to
> a lot of sources
> in the same college which will lead to severa

Hello everybody:
The multiple contacts are bound to be there. However, we can have a tacit
in-house understanding. Depending on the stature of the College persons and
the time-availability of the LUG guys [why no gals?], we can allow one of
our group to take the lead -- often one dealing with the topmost person.
Sometimes, it is difficult to get the top guy regularly -- so you get an
intro to the 'active contacts' in the college and work thru them.

e.g., in Arunai, to get the goahead you should speak to the Chairman [since
Mr. Velu has become Food Minister, his son has taken over], but for getting
things done you have to talk to the PRO Suresh. In many colleges it is
Chairman or Director, rarely it is the Principal and for getting things
actually done, we have to keep the HoD CSE or IT (which one?).

As for Jaya Engg, Aanjhan can apprise the Chairman, bring Kumaran into the
picture and then Shakthi-Kumaran combine can take over. [this is just a
suggestion -- please do as you guys deem fit]. The Principal is originally
from MIT (Mech Engg) and if anything is needed from him, we can talk to him.

Because of the NRCFOSS training  -- and our mandate to push in the elective
-- we are in regular touch with a large no of colleges / teachers. My
earlier stint at Arunai adds more members to this pool -- during my stay
around 20 lecturers resigned and went to different colleges . I have been
coaxing the colleges to conduct LDDs / workshop to create awareness.

I will do the following : do some initial interactions (mostly thru our
au-kbc mails) -- keep Parthan in the picture and once the date/program is
fixed, let him take over. Please keep in mind that many colleges would like
to have some 'VIP(!)' presence to inaugurate the show. I will try to do my
bit in the background -- whether initiated thru NRCFOSS or directly thru
LUG.

With best wishes, Srinivasan.

On 7/12/06, Bharath Narayan <bharath144@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> hi all,
>
> i want to know the execution time of a program.
> what method can i use to do this?


You could put your command into time{command}.

For example,
*time { ./configure ... && make && make install; }*.

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Wed Jul 12 18:15:05 2006
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Wed Jul 12 18:15:14 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Tamil on Debian Sarge
Message-ID: <a0c4f6270607120545x47c53a29q94abb735ead9e336@mail.gmail.com>

Dear ILUGC,

After Mr.Thyagarajan's talk and Shakthi's demo, I spent some time with
Debian Sarge, trying to get Indian languages to work. I wanted to
inform you that upon installing the package tamil-gtk2im and following
the readme in the package, Tamil works flawlessly on GTK based
applications, including Mozilla Firefox. The key is bound, by default,
to double shift (meaning press both shift keys together).

So, do try it out. Also, it'd be nice if someone could test Suse and
Fedora Core, as they are also bound to have this feature.

??? Debian Sarge????? ??????? ???? ??????? ???????????!

HTH. The advice was from the Debian developer, R.Ganesan.

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Wed Jul 12 18:16:46 2006
From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (R.Ramkumar)
Date: Wed Jul 12 18:16:59 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] program execution time
In-Reply-To: <d6e7f37f0607120432u714ac366yb6830f1b3d40b829@mail.gmail.com>
References: <c0b743a40607120245m4665035dod840a1c96372ab2a@mail.gmail.com>
	<44B4C6FE.3060706@aim.com> <44B4C76E.2000307@aim.com>
	<c0b743a40607120305o3ac63b7aucbdb2d0843af7ef2@mail.gmail.com>
	<9a9bfc170607120349w358f887fl9758ecf89dc1725b@mail.gmail.com>
	<d6e7f37f0607120432u714ac366yb6830f1b3d40b829@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <9a9bfc170607120546l4fa9c48bybb206d1a14f226f8@mail.gmail.com>

> This will not work.. i have tried time() function of C. It will not come up
> to nanosecond precision because it returns time_t short int..
> use clock function, it will give the processing time..or times() function..

What do you mean by `time' will not work? Every timing function has
it's precision, and for the function I gave, it was one second. The OP
had never given any idea of the precision needed, and hence I
preferred the most portable one. There are many other functions which
allow for more accurate representations but at the cost of
portability. for eg. many versions of FreeBSD do not conform to the
SUSv2 spec for the `clock' function you specified. Secondly,
representations upto a nanosecond (like struct timespec) never
guaranteed you a nanosecond precision. Various functions allow you to
get timing details as accurate as the OS can allow, but the precisions
reached are rarely to a nanosecond. These precision depend on the OS
and the hardware which form the clock sources for the OS.

it moves on...

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Wed Jul 12 07:21:53 2006

Subject: [Ilugc] July Month ILUGC Meeting

Hi Srinivasan and others,

--- Srinivasan Sundararajan <srini.it@gmail.com>
wrote:
> The multiple contacts are bound to be there.

... and it is essential. It helps in colleges when you
try to explain to different kinds of people from
different ends. They are usually ignorant.

> we can allow one of
> our group to take the lead -- often one dealing with
> the topmost person.

There should be no _single_ point of contact. I'll
tell you why.

Singapore LUG, for example, has elections and office
bearers. So, you hold a position for a year. 

But, in a year you might have lot of work that might
coincide with the time of LDDs. So, you may not be
able to do justice to both. Instead, if you keep the
contacts floating and use the mailing list as a point
of contact, whoever is available during the LDD time
_and_ willing to participate can contribute. The
probability of not getting someone is much less.

This has worked for many of our ILUGC members. There
were times when we did two workshops on a single day
by splitting our work.

http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/2005

> Sometimes, it is difficult to get the top guy
> regularly -- so you get an
> intro to the 'active contacts' in the college and
> work thru them.

You can approach the top guy as a AU-KBC or NRC-FOSS
member. As an individual, I can only contact
faculty/students and ask them to get permission in
their college for workshops - whatever be the
formalities.

And its easier to contact students/faculty through
e-mail/phone than the college management, from my
experience.
 
> As for Jaya Engg, Aanjhan can apprise the Chairman,
> bring Kumaran into the
> picture and then Shakthi-Kumaran combine can take
> over. 

Should be Saturday, July 22, 2006. Will get
confirmation soon.

> Please keep in mind that
> many colleges would like
> to have some 'VIP(!)' presence to inaugurate the
> show. 

These things should change. As an NRC-FOSS, AU-KBC
person, I am sure you guys have the power to change
such things.

It is the students' show. Let one of their own
inaugurate it.

For all the hard-work that Arunai Engineering College
students put it, I really wanted one of their own to
inaugurate it. 

Regards,

SK

On Wed, 12 Jul 2006, Sasikumar Murthy wrote:
> Thanks Sriram, This is genuine email only, otherwise how come i would
> send email to the administration from the respective email id.

anyone can send mail to the list admin with ANY from address. would you 
like for me send you a mail with your mail as the from address? done. you 
should have received it already. so, someone could play a prank on you by 
unsubscribing you from the list and i have no way to tell if the request 
is genuine or a prank; i cannot use the from address in the mail as proof 
of genuineness. however, your replying to my mail does constitute proof of 
genuineness since i sent my mail only to your address (and no one else can 
receive it) and only you (or someone with access to your mail account) can 
reply to its contents.

> Please do something to stop this chain emails for my email id.

these are not chain emails. ilugc is a legitimate mailing list that has 
been in existance for about 8 years now.

> Otherwise i will talk to IT person and want to take the necessary action
> against your group.

first off, dont issue such meaningless threats. i would have been happy to 
unsubscribe you once i have established the genuineness of your request. 
but if you want to issue such threats, i am not inclined to do so. you may 
unsubscribe yourself. go ahead and talk to your IT person. perhaps, your 
IT person can make more sense of this mail and explain to you what is 
happening.

> According to my knowledge i know that i havn't give my email id in any
> of the websites like this.

perhaps, this email id was earlier used by someone else (who subscribed to 
this list)? you cannot get on this mailing list by giving your email id 
anywhere. there is one and only one way to get on this list. you have to 
first make a request (by mail or through the web); in response to this 
request, you will receive a confirmation request stating that a request to 
subscribe has been received and subscription to the list will be effected 
only if you reply to this confirmation request. so, it is not possible for 
anyone to subscribe you without your knowledge. perhaps, an earlier owner 
of this id was subscribed to the list - but then the account became 
inactive or was disabled, causing mails to bounce. as a courtesy to list 
members, we periodically re-activate bouncing mail addresses and if they 
continue to bounce, the addresses are deleted from the subscriber list. in 
your case, it would appear that the account was only temporarily bouncing, 
so mail service has resumed.

-- 
sriram

perhaps, this email id was earlier used by someone else (who subscribed to
this list)? you cannot get on this mailing list by giving your email id
anywhere. there is one and only one way to get on this list. you have to
first make a request (by mail or through the web); in response to this
request, you will receive a confirmation request stating that a request to
subscribe has been received and subscription to the list will be effected
only if you reply to this confirmation request. so, it is not possible for
anyone to subscribe you without your knowledge. perhaps, an earlier owner
of this id was subscribed to the list - but then the account became
inactive or was disabled, causing mails to bounce. as a courtesy to list
members, we periodically re-activate bouncing mail addresses and if they
continue to bounce, the addresses are deleted from the subscriber list. in
your case, it would appear that the account was only temporarily bouncing,
so mail service has resumed.

--
sriram

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Thu Jul 13 10:28:57 2006
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Jul 13 19:59:09 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] help regarding powerpc and vga card
In-Reply-To: <44B6077E.9090004@gmail.com>
References: <44B6077E.9090004@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f990120607130728l1c16e3d2k6b1a09a02c1ed0f3@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/13/06, sudheer <urwithsudheer@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
>
> Anyone please help me if i am missing anything.
>
>     All PCI VGA cards for use on x86 PCs have a ROMscan BIOS
extension on them. This initializes the card after POST - basically,
the motherboard BIOS transfers control to the BIOS on the
PCI VGA card, which then initializes itself. If control is not
transfered to the VGA BIOS on the card, the VGA controller
stays isolated and will not respond to PCI device enumeration,
etc. This is actually part of the PC-98 spec., which allows
multiple VGA controllers to co-exist on the PCI and/or AGP
bus.

   On a PowerPC system, the ROMscan BIOS cannot execute
(because it has x86 instructions in it), so there will be an alternate
way to initialize the VGA controller so that it can respond to the
PCI enumeration, etc. However, that method will be card/controller
specific - neither the card manufacturer nor ATI may ever have
released the specs for how this is done. Usually, it will be through
hidden memory-mapped IO (MMIO) registers on the VGA controller
chip, but there are numerous proprietary ways to implement this,
most of it being undocumented or controller-specific.

(Lots of things are taken for granted in the x86 PC world, which
are actually very complex and difficult-to-implement protocols.
That's one of the reasons why all the alternative PC processor
architectures have failed over the last 20 years).

-Siva
From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Thu Jul 13 10:46:01 2006
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Jul 13 20:16:09 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] VMware as well as Virtual PC now free-as-in-free beer
Message-ID: <a8f990120607130746l586ca3f6teaa4aa1f0a865827@mail.gmail.com>

Folks,
         FWIW, both VMware server as well as M$ Virtual PC
are free-as-in-free-beer downloads starting this week. You may
have to register and provide some info, and you get free
license keys.

http://www.vmware.com/download/server/

http://www.microsoft.com/windows/virtualpc/default.mspx

The VMware server runs either on a Windows or a Linux box,
and allows multiple Windows or Linux clients. OTOH, the
Virtual PC only runs on a few M$ OSes like XP Pro, XP Server,
etc.

These provide full-virtualization layers, unlike the paravirtualization
hypervisor approach taken by Xen (which will not run any client OS
except specially-ported kernels).

Give VMware a try, it allows multiple Linux clients, which is great
for virtual hosting and other similar stuff.

-Siva

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Thu Jul 13 08:06:40 2006
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Thu Jul 13 20:36:52 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] help regarding powerpc and vga card
In-Reply-To: <44B6077E.9090004@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20060713150640.14063.qmail@web50202.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi Sudheer,

--- sudheer <urwithsudheer@gmail.com> wrote:
> PCI enumuration from 
> u-boot does not detect my VGA card whereas it
> detects other cards like 
> ethernet in the same slot.

Since, PCI is working fine with u-boot, you can write
a stand-alone main() routine to be run by u-boot to
read the PCI configuration space for the VGA card.
Check if you can read the vendor ID/device ID and that
the VGA controller is responding. If it works, you are
probably missing some configuration with u-boot for
your device.

http://www.xml.com/ldd/chapter/book/ch15.html

http://www.tldp.org/LDP/tlk/dd/pci.html

On 7/13/06, Sivasankar Chander <siva.ilugc@gmail.com> wrote:
>          FWIW, both VMware server as well as M$ Virtual PC
> are free-as-in-free-beer downloads starting this week.

VMPlayer has been free for use for many months now.  VMPlayer
has the same virtualization technology as VMWare Server, but
the user interface is simplistic.  VMPlayer also supported Intel
VT before VMWare Server, and is a 10 x smaller download (25MB).

Originally VMPlayer was intended to only run VMs created with
other VMWare products, but sites like www.easyvmx.com made
it possible to create VMs for free.  I'm yet to out growVMPlayer
and switch to VMWare Server.

I have not tried Virtual PC and would appreciate any comments.

I would gladly recommend everyone to give virtualization a go.
Having a VM is handy when you want to test different OSes or
create "clean room" development or demo environments.  I have
VMs for OpenSolaris, Debian, Win2k, Free/Open BSD on my
development box.

- Raja

From sriram at ae.iitm.ac.in  Fri Jul 14 11:34:35 2006
From: sriram at ae.iitm.ac.in (Prof. P. Sriram)
Date: Fri Jul 14 11:34:37 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] the list shrinketh
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0607141129460.16303@gateway.ae.iitm.ac.in>

dear cluggies,

i noticed recently that the list was having a lot of bouncing addresses
subscribed; these bouncing addresses automatically had mail delivery
suspended. to prune the list, i re-enabled delivery to all bouncing
addresses and those that continued to bounce have now been deleted from
the list. in case you were subscribed using such a bouncing mail address
(and presumably were using a web interface to read the messages), you may
find that you have now been deleted from the list (so, you will not longer
be able to post). please use only a valid and live mail address to sign on
to this list. with this pruning, our membership has shrunk from over 2000
to about 1300 (yeah, thats how many bouncing addresses we had).

-- 
sriram, list admin

for(Device = 0; Device <32; Device++){
        printf("\ndevice %d", Device);
         for(Function =0;Function <8;Function++){
            dev = PCI_BDF(BusNum, Device, Function);
            pci_read_config_word(dev, PCI_VENDOR_ID, &VendorID);
            if (VendorID != 0xFFFF){
                    printf("\nFound PCI device %02x.%02x.%02x:    ",

Subject: [Ilugc] help regarding powerpc and vga card

Hello Sivasankar,

Sivasankar Chander wrote:

>
>
> On 7/13/06, *sudheer* <urwithsudheer@gmail.com 
> <mailto:urwithsudheer@gmail.com>> wrote:
>
>
>
>     Anyone please help me if i am missing anything.
>
>     All PCI VGA cards for use on x86 PCs have a ROMscan BIOS
> extension on them. This initializes the card after POST - basically,
> the motherboard BIOS transfers control to the BIOS on the
> PCI VGA card, which then initializes itself. If control is not
> transfered to the VGA BIOS on the card, the VGA controller
> stays isolated and will not respond to PCI device enumeration,
> etc. This is actually part of the PC-98 spec., which allows
> multiple VGA controllers to co-exist on the PCI and/or AGP
> bus.
>
>    On a PowerPC system, the ROMscan BIOS cannot execute
> (because it has x86 instructions in it), so there will be an alternate
> way to initialize the VGA controller so that it can respond to the
> PCI enumeration, etc. However, that method will be card/controller
> specific - neither the card manufacturer nor ATI may ever have
> released the specs for how this is done. Usually, it will be through
> hidden memory-mapped IO (MMIO) registers on the VGA controller
> chip, but there are numerous proprietary ways to implement this,
> most of it being undocumented or controller-specific.

Thanks for your information.
Could anyone please suggest me which  vga card i need to buy so that it 
can be supported
 with powerpc boards and available in the market. Or can i have any 
other alternative solution .

Thanks  & Regards
Sudheer

>
> (Lots of things are taken for granted in the x86 PC world, which
> are actually very complex and difficult-to-implement protocols.
> That's one of the reasons why all the alternative PC processor
> architectures have failed over the last 20 years).
>
> -Siva

"..There's one other thing I should say. It's a very general thing.
Governments that impose harsh restrictions on their citizens, backed
up by cruel punishments, on behalf of corporations, are showing that
they are not really on the citizens's side. They're not working for
us, they don't represent us except with lip service. They represent
the corporations and their goal is to rule us. These governments are
democratic only in name. And since governments get their legitimacy
from ruling on behalf of the people and protecting the people's
rights, these governments lose their legitimacy.

I'm very sad to say that almost all governments around the World have
done this. "Government of the people, by the flunkies, for the
corporations". And it makes me very sad" (Stallman at

On 7/14/06, Sivasankar Chander <siva.ilugc@gmail.com> wrote:

>    Yup, I'll second this. Somebody also needs to tell Elcot to drop
> their IBM mainframe purchase for running Linux/S390 in VMs and
> go with x86 server clusters running Linux/x86 guests in VMware
> instead. They can even benchmark and test this inexpensively
> with free licenses - a Dell SC430 dual-core at Rs.18k should be
> enough to get started on the HW side.

I am not very sure, but here are my thoughts. IBM Z Series'
virtualization is, called as an
LPAR(http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LPAR). Though the virtualization is
full virtualization, but, I personally found, through  reports from
friends who actually did a performance analysis by deploying more than
1000 instances of Linux kernal, back in 2003, on a single Z/Server, in
addition to the Z/OS and other environments already running, that
IBM's virtualization is in fact, much better in terms of performances.

I think the packaging is what makes it more attractive. You can simply
go ahead and pull out two SMPS, 10 hard drives, one set of RAM and One
Air conditioning Unit out of the server and the server still runs
without a hitch (no restarting). This might sound familiar to those
who have attended Mr. Mark Dalton's session on SATA Hard disks, Blade
servers and Cray Super
computers(http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/Mark_Daltons_talk_-_Cray_XD1%2C_SATA%2C_Volume_management%2C_filesystems).

For an enterprise server for the size of TamilNadu (entire database
and ALL applications of ALL departments), I will not buy your
suggestion. The servers for such huge applications with 24x7
availability should be stored in specialized data centers, with
specialized cooling equipments built into them. I don't think you can
get that kind of cooling for an array of servers, and that can run for
months, if not for years, without restarting, for a mere 18,000
rupees..... I doubt, if enterprises like Tamil Nadu (with so much of
bureaucracy), will be ready/able to do such experiments, and draw
conclusions from their own experiments. They will surely buy the
solution, if already made by others and published. Perhaps DELL
themselves should do the experiment and sell the solution to TN.

Please correct me where I have misunderstood the requirements.


Regards,
Natarajan.
From parth.technofreak at gmail.com  Fri Jul 14 21:50:40 2006
From: parth.technofreak at gmail.com (Parthan)
Date: Fri Jul 14 21:51:02 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Doubt with Calling/Deeveloping OSS
Message-ID: <44B7C458.9030801@gmail.com>

Hello,
I ended up having a doubt about calling something OSS and using some 
widely available OS tools to build something whose source code you don't 
release. This is an advent of participating in a demonstration of a 
software package which is made 90% using OSS like PostgreSQL, etc. but 
the source code is not given along with.

Case Points:
1. The software uses many Open Source Tools available widely for use, 
example: PostgreSQL, Python etc.

2. The software openly declares it is making use of OSS fully.

3. The developer accepts he hasn't done any significant 'value-addition' 
to the individual sofwares he used as well as the combination of them.

4. Though he uses OSS for his overall development, he doesn't to release 
the source code. He intelligently never terms the software to be OSS, 
rather just says he is using 100% OSS and tools.

5. The sodtware is priced at an acceptable price suitable for Indian 
medium and small scale industries, mainly because all the pieces which 
make up the software as a whole is available free as in 'beer'

My questions are:

1. If someone is going to use some Open Source Tool and develop 
something (which he accepts doesnt have much value addition), is it 
right to hide the source code from the users who pay and buy the software ?

2. Though having a price tag is not opposed OSS, but restricting the 
main freedom to have source code, is it not condemnable ??

3. Isn't it ethically wrong to make use of OSS and in return give 
nothing to the OSS ?? :-S :(

-- 
With Regards

Parthan ('technofreak')

Research Assistant @ NRC-FOSS and Python\PHP Developer
A Proud Tuxian and an Ubuntero

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Fri Jul 14 12:49:52 2006
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Fri Jul 14 22:20:03 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] help regarding powerpc and vga card
In-Reply-To: <44B76B28.8080200@gmail.com>
References: <44B6077E.9090004@gmail.com>
	<a8f990120607130728l1c16e3d2k6b1a09a02c1ed0f3@mail.gmail.com>
	<44B743C1.10506@gmail.com> <44B76B28.8080200@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f990120607140949h259b430cjc0e231e4dd9454cd@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/14/06, sudheer <urwithsudheer@gmail.com> wrote:
>
>
> I have a doubt here. How does the processor know that the card  sitting
> here is a vga card
> and control should be transfered to initialize it.


   The processor (in an x86 PC) doesn't actually know that there's
a VGA controller in that PCI slot. However, the VGA ROM BIOS
is in a well-known range - usually 0xC0000 upwards. The PC ROM
BIOS does a quick presence check to see if there's a valid ROM
extension at 0xC0000, does a checksum and then just transfers
control to 0xC0000. At this point, the VGA ROM BIOS gets
control and does everything to initialize the VGA controller and
make it respond to PCI bus activity. Then it returns control to
PC ROM BIOS, which then repeats the exercise for other
memory ranges, like 0xD0000, etc. (where there may be other
ROM extensions, like a Network Boot ROM on a LAN card, etc.)

 I think it can know
> that it is a vga card only by reading the config space .
> And bios is necesary for vga card to work in its normal way. Is it
> necesary for bios to be initialised to get detected.
> Please correct me if i am wrong.


  Remember, an x86 PC with any PCI VGA card still works fine with
an OS like MS-DOS-3.3, which knows nothing about PCI - it was
written before the PCI spec was developed. A VGA card must
work correctly in some default mode, with a text-mode character
buffer at a well-known MMIO range, and functioning ASCII-to-
character glyph mapping. All this is taken care off by the VGA BIOS
ROM sitting on the VGA card - which initializes the controller to
the default text mode when it gets control after POST. That's
also the reason that the very first visible text message that you
see on powering up a PC is from the VGA BIOS, not the
motherboard ROM BIOS.

The reason for the VGA controller on an add-in PCI card to remain
inactive on POST, until it is initialized, is simple: there may be multiple
PCI VGA cards, and there would be bus contention for the text buffer
if they all initialized themselves to active on say, the reset signal. Also,
many boards have on-board integrated VGA (like the i810), and there
has to be a way of over-riding the off-board VGA(s) and leaving them
inactive, if so desired.

> Could anyone please suggest me which  vga card i need to buy so that
> > it can be supported
> > with powerpc boards and available in the market. Or can i have any
> > other alternative solution .
> >
>
     Back in the hoary old days of PREP and CHRP (IBM specifications
for PCs with PowerPC CPUs) reference implementations, there were
a handful of S3 cards which were supported by the PREP ROM
itself. However, you may want to ask the developer of the PowerPC
board about which VGA controllers are initialized correctly by the
PowerPC ROM BIOS code alone.

-Siva

On 7/14/06, benjamin <benjaminrtz@gmail.com> wrote:
> If one's running Linux guest's alone.. someone might as tell run Xen.

Running linux on linux for application/domain isolation does not
require full-virtualization layers as provided by VMWare/Xen.  The
RAM overhead of simultaneously running multiple OSes is just
too much.

Linux VServer (http://linux-vserver.org/) provides Solaris 10 Zones
like security contexts and allows adequate isolation between domains.
Incomarison to VMWare/Xen, or even User Mode Linux, the CPU and
RAM overheads are minimal.

- Raja

--- Natarajan V <rajanvn@gmail.com> wrote:

> 
> For an enterprise server for the size of TamilNadu (entire database
> and ALL applications of ALL departments), I will not buy your
> suggestion. The servers for such huge applications with 24x7
> availability should be stored in specialized data centers, with
> specialized cooling equipments built into them. I don't think you
> can
> get that kind of cooling for an array of servers, and that can run
> for
> months, if not for years, without restarting, for a mere 18,000
> rupees..... I doubt, if enterprises like Tamil Nadu (with so much
> of
> bureaucracy), will be ready/able to do such experiments, and draw
> conclusions from their own experiments. They will surely buy the
> solution, if already made by others and published. Perhaps DELL
> themselves should do the experiment and sell the solution to TN.

I am not technically competent to talk about virtualisation, Xen, IBM
servers etc.

However, based on my experience in Government way of working, Google
model is the best for govt. Why one huge common database for all
application - except possibly a huge citizen database. Most of the
government work can be split into several convenient independent
databases. Interaction among different department are very minimal.

In last nearly 20years of GOI working I have not seen a single
instance of huge data is really analysed and some decision taken.
Essentially, what is required a data storage, which can be retrieved,
mostly with point queries.

What people talk about e-governance with large enterprise grade ( and
other high sounding words) will have no use unless administrative
reforms are carried out, and drastic change is brought in procedures.

In my estimate even a very determined, honest ministers+top_officers
should take atleast 20 years to bring about the kind of unified
database that will truely mean e-governance. Until, that time,
building in pieces (however keeping the design centralised and
compatible) will be cost effective way.

I know serveral offices who have IBM/Solaris/HP servers worth
8-10lakhs storing 50% records of what I am storing on p3-PC.

In my opinion government should not rush in spending on hardware,
before really developing,testing application. Generally the
implementation time is very long, and the full power of system will
be required about 2-3 years after serious start of implementation.

Delay hardware procurement as much as possible to get best
price+technology.

Raman.P

was running okay. But today while booting it was directly taking me to grub
rompt. From prompt, I tried to boot by 'boot' command. It failed with this
error message
Error 16: Inconsistent filesystem structure.

After some googling I've found that this error is returned by filesystem
code to denote an internal error caused by the sanity checks of the
filesystem structure on disk not matching what it expects. So now my
question is does that mean my hard disk is gone! If so is there any way to
get back my data? btw my 80gb disk was partitioned as LVM.

Please help me in this regard.

From lawgon at thenilgiris.com  Sun Jul 16 12:56:14 2006

Subject: [Ilugc] Doubt with Calling/Deeveloping OSS
In-Reply-To: <44B7C458.9030801@gmail.com>
References: <44B7C458.9030801@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <D8B7E403-03FA-46DD-BC39-223BD5C9D1F6@thenilgiris.com>


On 14-Jul-06, at 9:50 PM, Parthan wrote:

> I ended up having a doubt about calling something OSS and using  
> some widely available OS tools to build something whose source code  
> you don't release. This is an advent of participating in a  
> demonstration of a software package which is made 90% using OSS  
> like PostgreSQL, etc. but the source code is not given along with.

foss is a child of the internet, and the main foss tool is the  
internet. In order, foss tools are:

1. mailing lists
2. forums
3. repositories
5. bugtrackers
6. wikis

all of which are publicly accessible (at least read, usually not  
write). Just because a software package is developed using foss  
packages, it does not lend any particular foss 'vaadai' to the package.

The power and stability of the foss model is due to public access to  
these tools in development. So a developer who is not using these  
tools cannot claim he is using foss tools for development. Nothing  
wrong with writing and selling good closed source software, but to  
try to push it by giving a foss halo round it is bad. And they cant  
prove it anyway as they wont show the code. I can say that M$ access  
is written with foss tools - can anyone disprove it?

--

kg

From vamlists at gmail.com  Mon Jul 17 06:33:25 2006
From: vamlists at gmail.com (Vamsee Kanakala)
Date: Mon Jul 17 06:33:37 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] frameworks

Natarajan V wrote:
> On 7/15/06, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com> wrote:
>> hi,
>> in context of recent threads regarding frameworks and enterprise
>> level programming, this may be of interest:
>>
>> http://wiki.rubyonrails.com/rails/pages/Framework+Performance
>
Hmm. It's a given that Ruby's performance has always been slower than 
Python's. One would be surprised if Ruby were faster, because Python 
received a lot more attention through the years, and lot more people 
hacked on it, to make it faster.

Now, things have changed. YARV (a Ruby VM) is going into Ruby 1.9, it is 
supposed to make Ruby much, much faster. But the point of a web 
framework is not performance (though it's still very important). It's 
programmer productivity. The little difference in performance between 
Ruby vs. Python vs. Java can be easily covered with a little more 
powerful hardware (for regular use, I would go so far as to say that 
this difference doesn't matter).

But, the point of Rails (in some ways, Django too - just not to be 
partial) is the tremendous increase of programmer productivity it gives 
versus, say J2EE. I've been a Java/J2EE fanboy before, worked on open 
source frameworks like Struts & Spring, so I know the pain (in 
hindsight). From  personal experience, Rails has made me at least 5x 
faster (now I'll don my asbestos suit). And I actually like webapp 
deployment now (don't remind me about the hoops I used to jump through 
to get Apache + Tomcat running).

It's a whole new ballgame. Rails, Django, TurboGears (another python 
framework - this is very decent too - wonder why Python guys are not 
talking about it?) are competitors in this arena, so choose what you 
want and like out of these. Ahem, that's after you take a look at them 
yourself, of course ;-). Good luck!


Vamsee.

> powerful hardware (for regular use, I would go so far as to say that
> this difference doesn't matter).
>

Fully agree. Programmers are expensive and need to be pampered
frequently.  Machines do just what they are told to do -- no need for
appraisals, counselling... pay rises :-)

> It's a whole new ballgame. Rails, Django, TurboGears (another python
> framework - this is very decent too - wonder why Python guys are not
> talking about it?) are competitors in this arena, so choose what you
> want and like out of these. Ahem, that's after you take a look at them
> yourself, of course ;-). Good luck!
>

Then there is 'trails' for java (IMO and unfortunate choice for a
project name!).

It is not so much the underlying language that is great about Rails
(of course, if you are from a java background you cannot fail to
notice the drastic reduction in the number of lines of code needed to
implement any functionality in ruby) but the fresh approach to
framework design. In other frameworks, one had to write (and write)
dozens of configuration files to get something working. But in Rails,
there is a default for almost everything and you need to configure
only those variables that need tweaking for your specific
functionality.

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Mon Jul 17 13:23:38 2006
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Mon Jul 17 13:22:59 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Python and Ruby Frameworks vs Statically typed languages
Message-ID: <1389.61.247.255.57.1153122818.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>But, the point of Rails (in some ways, Django too - just not to be
>partial) is the tremendous increase of programmer productivity it gives
>versus, say J2EE. I've been a Java/J2EE fanboy before, worked on open
>source frameworks like Struts & Spring, so I know the pain (in
>hindsight).

I agree with you that these frameworks are far simpler to use than J2EE.
However, one of the problems I have noticed with these frameworks has
nothing to do with the frameworks themselves but rather with the
dynamically-typed nature of Python and Ruby which makes it very difficult
to catch some errors.

For very large applications, it is best to use a language which does not
have dynamic typing turned on by default.

There are ways of getting around this limitation ofcourse - such as
writing a whole range of unit test scripts for each and every aspect of
the solution. But in my experience, that is easier said than done because
it is almost impossible to unit-test some blocks of code such as UI
handling code.

Also, if I were to use unit-tests to get around this problem, it is in
anycase just a work around to a problem with the platform. This problem is
perhaps more elegantly solved if Python / Ruby includes a run-time switch
which turns of dynamic typing (but this will require fairly extensive
changes in these platforms).

I use statically-typed languages for coding for the same reason I set the
compiler preferences to display even very minor warnings when I develop in
C/C++; it is best to catch variable type errors at compile time rather
than at run-time.

Thanks,
Prem Kurian Philip

From vamlists at gmail.com  Mon Jul 17 15:52:00 2006
From: vamlists at gmail.com (Vamsee Kanakala)
Date: Mon Jul 17 15:52:14 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Python and Ruby Frameworks vs Statically typed languages
In-Reply-To: <1389.61.247.255.57.1153122818.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
References: <1389.61.247.255.57.1153122818.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
Message-ID: <44BB64C8.9020604@gmail.com>

Prem Kurian Philip wrote:
> I agree with you that these frameworks are far simpler to use than J2EE.
> However, one of the problems I have noticed with these frameworks has
> nothing to do with the frameworks themselves but rather with the
> dynamically-typed nature of Python and Ruby which makes it very difficult
> to catch some errors.
>
> For very large applications, it is best to use a language which does not
> have dynamic typing turned on by default.
>
>   

Oh boy. The age-old dynamic vs. static typing argument. Check out the 
recent comp.lang.lisp threads for a particularly long-drawn discussion 
on this. They are much more detailed and make valid technical points on 
both sides better than I can.

> There are ways of getting around this limitation ofcourse - such as
> writing a whole range of unit test scripts for each and every aspect of
> the solution. But in my experience, that is easier said than done because
> it is almost impossible to unit-test some blocks of code such as UI
> handling code.
>
>   
I don't know about desktop apps - but UI testing would be overkill for 
most webapps. Validation checks, yes - but writing unit tests for how a 
certain div will appear on your html page will quickly bog you down. A 
good web designer is all you need. So I would consider this a moot point.

> Also, if I were to use unit-tests to get around this problem, it is in
> anycase just a work around to a problem with the platform. This problem is
> perhaps more elegantly solved if Python / Ruby includes a run-time switch
> which turns of dynamic typing (but this will require fairly extensive
> changes in these platforms).
>
>   
Sorry, I have to strongly disagree. Just because you have static typing, 
it doesn't mean that you don't need unit testing at all. In that case, 
you wouldn't have JUnit, and all those XP methodologies and tools to 
make Java projects a little more manageable.

Unit tests are written mainly for things like clarifying design (when 
you do TDD, you will be surprised how many design flaws you find 
beforehand), enabling change (smaller feedback loops between coder and 
customer) and finally, to create a strong test suite (so that new 
changes don't break old code) - so as to enable better integration 
testing and the likes.

> I use statically-typed languages for coding for the same reason I set the
> compiler preferences to display even very minor warnings when I develop in
> C/C++; it is best to catch variable type errors at compile time rather
> than at run-time.
>
>   
Yes, it would be nice to have the type errors flagged beforehand. But, 
type errors are one of the minor errors to worry about. You are going to 
find them sooner or later (either during unit tests or manual testing). 
What is more important to worry about is how fast you are able to 
market  your web product or how fast you are able to roll out the 
first-but-buggy version to your customer.

As we all know, release early and release often is a good strategy. You 
can always correct your mistakes in the second round. Static languages 
hobble you in this respect that you have the extra compilation step. 
Development becomes slower because you have to recompile the entire 
webapp or parts of it every time you make a change. Dynamic languages 
win in this respect that they will remove that extra unnecessary step - 
you're gonna write unit tests anyways (for the above reasons), so why 
slow you down with an extra step?

I know it can be argued both ways for quite a long time, but I think for 
now I support dynamic languages unless I really think they're 
compromising my web app. So far, I had no such complaints. In fact, I'm 
happier now because my compiler won't complain that I used a BigInt, 
SmallInt, WhateverInt instead of an Int. It's a friggin number dammit, 
now get on with it!

Well, this is where the subjectivity and religious wars come in - 
purists want type safety at any cost; pragmatists don't care about it 
until it hits them on their head - which it rarely does. I'm certainly 
in the latter camp.


Vamsee.

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Mon Jul 17 18:36:40 2006
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Mon Jul 17 18:35:58 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] RE: RE: Python and Ruby Frameworks vs Statically typed
	languages
Message-ID: <2329.61.247.255.57.1153141600.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

Hi Vamsee,

>> Also, if I were to use unit-tests to get around this problem, it is in
>> anycase just a work around to a problem with the platform. This problem is
>> perhaps more elegantly solved if Python / Ruby includes a run-time switch
>> which turns of dynamic typing (but this will require fairly extensive
>> changes in these platforms).
>>
>>
>Sorry, I have to strongly disagree. Just because you have static typing,
>it doesn't mean that you don't need unit testing at all. In that case,
>you wouldn't have JUnit, and all those XP methodologies and tools to
>make Java projects a little more manageable.

I didn't make the assertion that unit tests are not needed. What I said is
that using unit tests to find errors which could have been caught during a
normal compilation stage is kludgy. Unit tests are good and have their
place, but a compile time error listing is definitely a useful aid.

>Well, this is where the subjectivity and religious wars come in -
>purists want type safety at any cost; pragmatists don't care about it
>until it hits them on their head - which it rarely does. I'm certainly
>in the latter camp.

If your application is simple, and it is not mission critical, then it is
perhaps useful to go with the line of reasoning that you expound here -
that is to discount errors which "rarely" occur. A compile time warning or
error is definitely a wonderful mechanism to detect errors which might
otherwise be very difficult to detect.

I have written and architected some very large enterprise applications in
Python: if I am asked to do something similar now, I would definitely go
with a language like Java. The problem with java is not the language but
rather the overly complicated mess that is J2EE and this crazy fixation
with "descriptive programming" using a million XML files for even
describing application logic. J2EE looks like it was designed by a
committee and it most certainly was.

The time it takes to compile code is quite often overstated. The compile
process reveals errors which can then be fixed quite easily. In a
dynamically-typed system, you will have to deal with the same errors but
you will discover them (if at all) only at runtime - and so what you lose
in compile time (on statically typed languages) is more than exceeded in
time it takes to discover the errors while programming using a
dynamically-typed language.

Also, the performance penalty of dynamically-typed languages may not be
suitable for some applications.

I am no purist - I continue to use languages like Python and Ruby (and on
occassion, groovy), but not for the large scale applications where java /
.net is more suitable.

Thanks,
Prem

On 7/17/06, Vamsee Kanakala <vamlists@gmail.com> wrote:
> As we all know, release early and release often is a good strategy. You
> can always correct your mistakes in the second round.

What you just said is very true from developer perspective.. but...

I would like to strongly contradict you on this. In huge enterprises,
with hundreds of equally huge applications deployed in production,
"release often" is least preferred. Each deployment cycle takes up
huge resources(Time and human efforts), in terms of re-testing the
entire application, re-training naive users (if applicable),
maintaining downtimes (for 24x7 applications), etc... So, many times,
the IT managers prefer to "catch" all the bugs before the first
deployment, and for each and every release, they try to squeeze in as
many new/fix features as possible, so that, they can reduce another
deployment cycle.

The situation becomes worse, when it comes to desktop
(non-centralized) applications.

 This is wrt Enterprise application programs. But when it comes to
product development (including FOSS), release often and release early
is ofcourse prefered from the developer point of view.
From rajasuperman at gmail.com  Mon Jul 17 22:09:58 2006
From: rajasuperman at gmail.com (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Mon Jul 17 22:10:07 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] desktop hardware recommendations -- was (no subject)
Message-ID: <92f9a9560607170939ke137a0ar627c74908e3e8e91@mail.gmail.com>

On 17 Jul 2006 14:31:47 -0000, Nagappan L <nagappan_l@rediffmail.com> wrote:
> I am planning to purchase a desktop system (Linux comp).
>

Buy the best monitor, keyboard and mouse your budget will allow.
See, touch and feel these 3 items before purchasing.  I would
recommend a TVS Gold mechanical keyboard, and a comfortable
Logitech or Microsoft mouse that fits your hand.

Consider an LCD monitor if possible.  Visit dpreview.com to
understand how your monitor shows various colors.

Buy atleast 512MB RAM (helps when you run vmware/xen/etc),
1GB RAM is preferred.

Purchase a Seagate HDD of atleast 120GB capacity.  IMO
Seagagte has better reliability than Maxtor, Samsung, etc.

Get a decent UPS.

Ensure all other hardware you get (video, audio, nic, etc) are
are supported out of the box.  Unsupported hardware is a pain.

Depending on your workload, any modern CPU should do so
I would give it the least importance.  Intel VT-x (found on Conroe)
is nice as it allows you to run an unmodified OS (WinXP) as a
Xen guest.  If you dont need this feature, buy a Celeron or Sempron.

Naturally, you will have to do some research before finalising on
your components, and from experience, it's usually good fun.
It will make you more informed about what you are purchasing
as a customer.

- Raja

PS: please add a sensible subject to your posts.

From vamlists at gmail.com  Tue Jul 18 00:27:48 2006
From: vamlists at gmail.com (Vamsee Kanakala)
Date: Tue Jul 18 00:27:58 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Python and Ruby Frameworks vs Statically typed languages
In-Reply-To: <e977d4310607170853g3b1be2cah251671e4645e3b37@mail.gmail.com>
References: <1389.61.247.255.57.1153122818.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>	
	<44BB64C8.9020604@gmail.com>
	<e977d4310607170853g3b1be2cah251671e4645e3b37@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <44BBDDAC.7080108@gmail.com>

Natarajan V wrote:
> In huge enterprises,
> with hundreds of equally huge applications deployed in production,
> "release often" is least preferred. Each deployment cycle takes up
> huge resources(Time and human efforts), 
Agile methodologies are targeted at reducing precisely the consumption 
of huge resources when you are deploying (and in other steps too). If 
you can reduce the amount of cost and effort that goes with each 
deployment, then frequent releases are a good thing, right?

> in terms of re-testing the
> entire application, 
If you have a really good test suite, this would not be much of an 
issue. This will work as your safety net when you are making changes to 
the code. You would not need to re-test the entire application. If you 
use continuous builds, it will be even more easier to manage this.

> re-training naive users (if applicable),
Whether naive or not, frequent changes in application does raise the 
specter of re-training, but mostly the changes will be small. Since we 
are talking about a few weeks or at most a month to do a new release, I 
don't think the functionality changes drastically between two releases. 
So, you wouldn't need to invest so much in training.

You can take this as an on-going thing. Every new release, you train the 
users for an hour or two,  let them work on the new features, take 
feedback, and work on the next release. This way, you wouldn't have to 
do huge 3-4 day training programs, at the end of which nobody is sure 
how much the users learned. Let's face it, most of us learn how to use a 
software on the fly, on the job.

> maintaining downtimes (for 24x7 applications), etc... So, many times,
> the IT managers prefer to "catch" all the bugs before the first
> deployment, and for each and every release, they try to squeeze in as
> many new/fix features as possible, so that, they can reduce another
> deployment cycle.
>
That is precisely the recipe for disaster in most 'enterprise' software. 
Lets face it, there is hardly any time to fix bugs when a release is 
looming. The major disadvantage is that, since the deployment cycles are 
so costly, there is less tendency to fix bugs after they miss the 
bug-fix phase. They are delayed until the next cycle, which causes 
endless cursing among the users.

> The situation becomes worse, when it comes to desktop
> (non-centralized) applications.
>
> This is wrt Enterprise application programs. But when it comes to
> product development (including FOSS), release often and release early
> is ofcourse prefered from the developer point of view.
>

Frequent releases make sense in most scenarios, except maybe in places 
like avionics software, or other real-time applications where having 
bugs can be quite costly in many fronts. In which case, obviously there 
would be a lot of pre-release testing. Also because specs stay the same 
for an entire model of a fighter jet, for quite some years.

In a business scenario the requirements change every quarter. The 
business changes, its competitors change, so the software has to change 
to cater to that need. Here, having long-drawn release cycles is quite 
bad, and that's why enterprise software projects (I read somewhere that 
it's as high as 70%) have such a high rate of  failure. They become 
obsolete before they even get deployed.

It maybe true that the scenario you explained exists in many enterprise 
software shops, and that's precisely the reason why they should move to 
Agile development methodologies.


Vamsee.

> I don't get it - are you saying that you write unit tests in Java to
> handle its' type errors/dynamicity? Then it's certainly news to me - in
> all the agile books and articles I read, I've never seen this reason
> before.

afaik, unit tests are written not just for typing errors but for a
whole lot of reasons. it is just that the need for such tests
increases by quite a bit when the language is dynamically typed, coz
many of the type related bugs are not caught at compile time. my point
is that, under the hypothetical (note :) ) situation where the only
need for unit tests are possible type errors, java is dynamically
typed enough to need them.

it moves on...

From girish1729 at yahoo.com  Mon Jul 17 22:02:58 2006
From: girish1729 at yahoo.com (Girish Venkatachalam)
Date: Tue Jul 18 10:33:18 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Commands in Linux..
In-Reply-To: <c0b743a40607172137u71dd5c77tc1fd86d867d3aa66@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20060718050258.78353.qmail@web35612.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

It is a very good question but unfortunately there is
no such command and there never will be. 

Let me try to explain why reality is so depressing.
:-)

1) There are several 10,000s of packages which are
installed on a case by case basis depending on one's
need. 

2) Some of the categories are listed below

archivers   cross          finance      mail       
news       shells
audio       crosspkgtools  sysutils
benchmarks  games        math        parallel   
biology     databases      geography    mbone      
pkglocate  textproc
bootstrap   devel          graphics     meta-pkgs  
pkgtools   time
cad         ham          misc        print      wm
chat        doc            inputmethod  mk         
README     www
comms       editors        lang         multimedia 
regress    x11
converters  emulators      licenses     net        
security

3) So you can see no one can know all commands. One
command in bash that can give you what you want is if
you press the <TAB> key twice

Display all 3594 possibilities? (y or n)

is what I get bcoz I have installed packages that give
me these many commands. 

But it is not humanly possible to learn all of them
nor is there a need. :-) You can however try "man
<cmd>" for whichever cmd that has a man page. 

4) New commands are being created every day, every
hour. Even you can create one. How will others know?
It will take time. 

If I understand your need correctly you have to learn
the various "shell commands". By this is meant common
small small tools used for day to day productivity. 

I will try to list some of them but this is by no

Subject: [Ilugc] Tamil keyboard driver needed
In-Reply-To: <dd680c2b0607082345j284c6a0dx432dca60a37c4df8@mail.gmail.com>
References: <dd680c2b0607082345j284c6a0dx432dca60a37c4df8@mail.gmail.com>

hi Shrini/Mugunth,


On 7/9/06, Shrinivasan T <tshrinivasan@gmail.com> wrote:
> Friends.
>
> ELCOT needs tamil keyboard layout 100% compitable with Remington layout.
> It is the one the ordinary tamil typewriter has.
> Because most of the government staff trained and certified by
> typewriting institutes as has more experience on that.

Had a conversation with Parimala of
our office on the Remignton typewriter layout.

The layout at:
http://www.tamilnation.org/images/digital/key2.jpg
is mostly correct representation of Tamil remington keyboard.
Some of the incorrect representations include:
"A" key (shift+a) should represent ?? (RA) as in ????  (puRA = pigeon)
"Z" key (shift+z) should represent ?? (NA) as in ????? (aNNA = elder brother)

Parimala has defined each of tamil character key in the
Remington typewriter layout in the attached file.
First column is the actual Tamil characters starting from
a, A, i, I ..... to Sri plus a few symbols (313 tamil chars + 9 symbols).
The second column is the
keystrokes in an Engish keyboard that need to be pressed
to get the column one tamil character or symbol.
(tamil chars in unicode) There are 4 characters for which
we are unsure about the keystrokes. They are indicated
according in the file. Will confirm later.

Let me know if you have issues in viewing the file.

hari.

ps: One issue that needs to be solved
in this layout is that the order in which
keystrokes are to entered is different from
the order in which it gets represented in Unicode.
eg: for ?? *mi*  ? (i)+?(ma) is keying order in remington layout
requirement, whereas unicode text has to be stored as
?(ma)+? (i).

From toufeeqh at gmail.com  Tue Jul 18 14:59:09 2006

Subject: [Ilugc] RE: RE: Python and Ruby Frameworks vs Statically typed
	languages
In-Reply-To: <2329.61.247.255.57.1153141600.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
References: <2329.61.247.255.57.1153141600.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
Message-ID: <c293dd340607180229n62fb2466raf2ef7937f82c839@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

On 7/17/06, Prem Kurian Philip <prem@songbirdtech.com> wrote:
> I have written and architected some very large enterprise applications in
> Python: if I am asked to do something similar now, I would definitely go
> with a language like Java. The problem with java is not the language but
> rather the overly complicated mess that is J2EE and this crazy fixation
> with "descriptive programming" using a million XML files for even
> describing application logic. J2EE looks like it was designed by a
> committee and it most certainly was.
>
> The time it takes to compile code is quite often overstated. The compile
> process reveals errors which can then be fixed quite easily. In a
> dynamically-typed system, you will have to deal with the same errors but
> you will discover them (if at all) only at runtime - and so what you lose
> in compile time (on statically typed languages) is more than exceeded in
> time it takes to discover the errors while programming using a
> dynamically-typed language.
>
> Also, the performance penalty of dynamically-typed languages may not be
> suitable for some applications.
>
> I am no purist - I continue to use languages like Python and Ruby (and on
> occassion, groovy), but not for the large scale applications where java /
> .net is more suitable.

Dr.Dobb tells me a different story.
http://www.ddj.com/dept/database/187203512

-Toufeeq
-- 
blog @ http://toufeeq.blogspot.com
From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Jul 18 15:09:34 2006
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)

Subject: [Ilugc] RE: RE: Python and Ruby Frameworks vs Statically typed

In-Reply-To: <c293dd340607180229n62fb2466raf2ef7937f82c839@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

>> I am no purist - I continue to use languages like Python and Ruby (and
>> on
>> occassion, groovy), but not for the large scale applications where java
>> /
>> .net is more suitable.
>
> Dr.Dobb tells me a different story.
> http://www.ddj.com/dept/database/187203512

Its wonderful that someone was able to port their application to Ruby on
Rails and benefit from that, but I have real difficulty believing
applications such as banking applications will ever get any real benefit
from being ported over to Ruby.

Note that the page you have linked to does not talk about the nature of
the application which was ported over - all it says is that 4 days of Ruby
coding was needed for porting over a Java application that took 4 months
to code.

Another critical fact to consider is that the first time you write an
application it is definitely going to take a long time - if this same
application were to be rewritten from scratch in Java (without reusing
existing code), would it take as long as it took to develop it the first
time around? what if this was rewritten for .NET?

Also, a 4 month Java project by 2 people (at most) hardly qualifies to be
called "large."

regards,
Prem

Subject: [Ilugc] [OT]Have you ever thought of the person who invented "CTRL
	+ ALT + DEL" key combination.
Message-ID: <20060718094708.18952.qmail@web30812.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

Have you ever thought of the person who invented "CTRL +   ALT + DEL" key combination. 
     
    "David Bradley"
    He is the One who spent 1 minute and 23 seconds in   writing the source code that rescues 
    the world's PC users for decades This extraordinary IBM   employee is retiring on 
    Friday, 25th March 2005 after a prolong service of 29   years. 
     
    His formula forces obstinate computers to restart when   they no longer follow other commands. 
     
    By 1980, Bradley was one of 12 people working to create   the debut. 
     
    The engineers knew they had to design a simple way to   restart the computer 
    when it fails to respond the user Bradley wrote the code   to make it work.
     
    Bradley says. "I did a lot of other things than   Ctrl-Alt-Delete, but I'm famous for that one."

create it! emacs21 searches for ~/.emacs.elc, ~/.emacs.el and
~/.emacs; in that order...

fyi, emacs22 (yet to be released, still in cvs) searches for ~/.emacs*
, ~/.emacs.d/.emacs* and ~/.emacs.d/init.el(c). So, what you did would
have worked there.

From mbchandar at gmail.com  Tue Jul 18 21:27:34 2006
From: mbchandar at gmail.com (balachandar muruganantham)
Date: Tue Jul 18 21:27:44 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Customizing Emacs21
In-Reply-To: <44BCB449.6040802@aim.com>
References: <20060718100854.41461.qmail@web8408.mail.in.yahoo.com>
	<44BCB449.6040802@aim.com>
Message-ID: <dc538c3f0607180857j2ccb061i387427653d375595@mail.gmail.com>

hi

On 7/18/06, Arun Velusamy <arunvelusamy@aim.com> wrote:
> Hi,
>     I am using emacs21 in my debian sarge machine.  I want to set
> syntax-highlighting(global-font-lock) on always.  I searched for .emacs
> file but i could only find ~/.emacs.d/ folder which doesnt have any
> files (except for auto-save-list folder).  I tried creating init.el
> file, but emacs didnt respond.

> Can anyone help me?

create .emacs in ur home directory

below are some of the basic settings which i use that u can put in ur .emacs

(require 'font-lock)
(global-font-lock-mode t)
for source code syntax highlighting

(setq make-backup-files nil)
no backup will be created

(setq inhibit-startup-message t)
no startup message

(transient-mark-mode t)
highlights when selecting(yanking)

(menu-bar-mode nil)
hide the top menu

(setq standard-indent 4)
indentation set for 4 space - set based upon u r programming language

(setq show-parens-mode t)
used for track starting and ending and highlighting braces in u r source code

(setq-default indent-tabs-mode nil)
indent based on tab

also u could add emacs to run on terminal using emacs -nw. for ease,
add in .bashrc

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Wed Jul 19 14:27:53 2006
From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (R.Ramkumar)
Date: Wed Jul 19 14:28:03 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Apostrophe display in firefox
In-Reply-To: <f789e6550607190115j7ed72057pe4960d1dcdfbdac3@mail.gmail.com>
References: <f789e6550607190115j7ed72057pe4960d1dcdfbdac3@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <9a9bfc170607190157x4d71cac4sa53e23f56d5918dc@mail.gmail.com>

>  Can anyone please tell me why " ' ", apostrophe, is getting displayed as "
> ? " in firefox browser. How can I rectify this? Im trying to get a few CGI

This is not a problem with firefox but with documents created using m$
word... Word considers it wise to replace quotes by what it calls
"smart quotes" (sic), where in a new character is replaced for the
starting and an another for the ending quote. This is not standard and
hence not all fonts support these characters (only the coding system
and ms' fonts in windows display them properly). The best solution for
this would be to use `tidy' with appropriate options to replace the
documents with less smarter, but saner quotes ;)

it moves on...

> Regarding Oo2.0, Linspire warehouse is not having Tamil locale Pack(rather

Hi Chakkaradeep,
>From the current version of OpenOffice(v 2.0.3) onwards, Tamil language pack
is made available by openoffice itself.
You can find the Tamil language pack (ta-IN) in this URL:
http://oootranslation.services.openoffice.org/pub/OpenOffice.org/2.0.3rc7/

Steps to install tamil pack:
1. Install english version of OpenOffice.org 2.0.3 first (you can get it
from http://download.openoffice.org/2.0.3/index.html )

2. Download and install the tamil language pack for your OS (seperate
language pack is available for linux/windows & Solaris) from
http://oootranslation.services.openoffice.org/pub/OpenOffice.org/2.0.3rc7/

3. Open the openoffice.org, go to
Tools --> Options --> Language Settings --> Languages
There there we can choose the Language of "User Interface".  Here Choose
Tamil,

4. Close OpenOffice and open again. now you should be able to see the
interface in tamil.

Please try and let us know if it works fine in Linspire..

From tech at leatherlink.net  Wed Jul 19 16:12:14 2006
From: tech at leatherlink.net (Ma Siva Kumar)
Date: Wed Jul 19 16:15:14 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Help with PostgreSQL (psycopg)
In-Reply-To: <44BDECDB.5060506@gmail.com>
References: <44BDECDB.5060506@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <200607191611.20289.tech@leatherlink.net>

Hi Parthan,

1. To get prompted for password when using psql try the following:
psql mydb --username guest --password

2. To always get password prompt change the authentication method in file  
/usr/local/pgsql/data/pg_hba.conf. (Assuming your installation is at 
/usr/local/pgsql). 

 'trust' will allow any user to connect as any other user by specifing 
--username option. 

3. I am not sure why your python script fails to connect. Are you running your 
python script in the same machine running the database server? 

If connecting over network, you should enable tcp/ip connection in 
postgresql.conf and allow permissions to the ip addresses in pg_hba.conf 
file. 

Best regards, 

Ma Sivakumar

On Wed July 19 2006 4:26 pm, you wrote:
> ------------------- pg_hba.conf-------------------------
> # Database administrative login by UNIX sockets
> local   all         postgres                          ident sameuser
>
> # TYPE  DATABASE    USER        CIDR-ADDRESS          METHOD
>
> # "local" is for Unix domain socket connections only
> local   all         all                               ident sameuser
> --------------------------------------------------------
>
> Should this be made into this ??
>
> ------------------- pg_hba.conf-------------------------
> # Database administrative login by UNIX sockets
> local   all         postgres                          ident sameuser
>
> # TYPE  DATABASE    USER        CIDR-ADDRESS          METHOD
>
> # "local" is for Unix domain socket connections only
> local   all         all                               trust
> --------------------------------------------------------

I guess so. Did you change this, restart postgresql and try connecting again? 

The set up 
"ident sameuser" means you can connect only as the user you are working as 
(unix loginname). With password or trust authentication, that restriction is 
gone and your script should work.

> > 3. I am not sure why your python script fails to connect. Are you running
> > your python script in the same machine running the database server?
>
> Nope, I am having PostgreSQL in my laptop in which I am working on
> Python. The gimmick needs to be found the first time, as I am pretty new
> to PostgreSQL and things aren't like MySQL.

After you are through with this do subscribe to pgsql-general@postgresql.org 
mailing list. 
One of the high quality tech lists I subscribe to. The discussions are always 
on topic, except when someone brings up MySQL :-). 

With PostgreSQL things are not like MySQL, they are far better. That is what 
the PostgreSQL developers and users believe. 

Best regards,

Ma Sivakumar
PS: You are not replying to the list. Use the reply all button in your mail 
client :-)

> > > Is it possible to download all the packages including dependencies
> > packages
> > > without installing with yum?
> > > I searched man pages but unable to find out any command.
> > > Can anybody point out how i will do this?
> > >
> >
> > # man rpm
> >
> > look for --aid option
> >
> >
> > --
> > Cheers,
> > Sivam
> > [Jai Hind]

>
>
>
> i mean to say when we do " yum install mplayer" ..yum will look yum repo
> and
> download and install the mplayer packages along with dependency pacages.
> My
> aim is to only download these pacages.
> I don't want to install.  I changed the /etc/yum.conf file [keepcache=1]
> and
> i could get all packages under /var/cache/yum/<repo name>/packagesor as
> specified . But the things is that after downloading this packages yum is
> going to  install these packages which i don't want. I can achive this by
> pressing ctrl+c before installion start . i don't want to watch when
> downloading of these packages has been finished ...............
>
> are there any [arg] available with yum which can do this thing?
>
> bye suman
> _______________________________________________
> To unsubscribe, email ilugc-request@ae.iitm.ac.in with
> "unsubscribe <password> <address>"
> in the subject or body of the message.
> http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/mailman/listinfo/ilugc
>

AFAIK, You can do that.. yum works with a python script.. After download, it
will run the installation as a transaction. You can see the script
/usr/bin/yum..

It calls.. yummain.py which is in /usr/share/yum-cli/
go to the section "Run the Transaction"
Comment the "base.doTransaction()" or add some code to ask for "y/N" before
doing this.

For sure that, some other easy ways too exist.. iam not recommending this..
go on with Google..

Suman Adak <ilugsuman@...> writes:
> hi list,
> 
> Is it possible to download all the packages including dependencies packages
> without installing with yum?

two solutions have been proposed, one using the rpm command and another
involving editing the yum python script itself - so, both are of limited use.
yum itself does not (yet?) support the download only option, but this option
becomes available if one installs the yum-utils package.

sriram

Hari, Parimala and their team successfully designed
a keyboard layuout for tamil as old typewriter layout.

-----------------------------------------------------------

hi Shrini,

Pl. see :
http://nrcfosshelpline.in/code/wiki/TamilRemingtonLayout

for instructions on installing Tamil remington on scim.
Sorry, I need to rush. Could'nt write the steps I did for
creating the scim tables. Essentially followed the steps
at :
http://www.scim-im.org/development/contribute/how_to_create_a_new_ime_in_about_15_minutes_with_scim_and_scim_tables
and used a modified form of the file I sent you yeterday.


-------------------------------------------------------------------


Hats off to the team.

This proves the power of open source and the community.
If there is no way, we would create our own.

Thanks for all wishers and contributors.

dear,
T.Shrinivasan.

From stylesen at gmail.com  Thu Jul 20 10:32:42 2006
From: stylesen at gmail.com (Senthil Kumaran S)
Date: Thu Jul 20 10:32:49 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Running my program at start up
In-Reply-To: <44BF0AD6.9010400@aim.com>
References: <44BF0AD6.9010400@aim.com>
Message-ID: <5ef2113c0607192202i3e49a8e9p6f11d05abba032d0@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/20/06, Arun Velusamy <arunvelusamy@aim.com> wrote:
>     I am using Debian sarge 3.1.  I want some of my programs ( say for
> eg., i have apache installed using tar.gz  in port 2000 ) to start at
> booting.  How could i acheive it?

In Debian sarge you can write your shell script to start these
services and put in /etc/init.d/
Do remeber to give +x to the script. Then
$ apt-get install rcconf
$ rcconf

After the above step you will find the script which you just added in
the list but it will be unchecked. Just check that script. Then it
will automatically start while booting.

If you use apt-get to install apache, the beautiful
packaging scripts will take care of starting it up for
u since 99% of users will want that. You can also
configure ur port and other things. 

If however for some reason u want a bleeding edge of
apache and u have compiled  it urself, u can always
use the update-rc.d script after creating a chota
shell script called apache.sh or something and putting
it under /etc/init.d

How-to unsubscribe if you forget your password

1. Goto page 
http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/mailman/options/ilugc

2. Give your email id, and press remind button. Your password will be
mailed to you.Open your mail and note the password.

3 Use this password and visit the page (as in 1 above) to unsubscribe

> Hi Chakkaradeep,
> From the current version of OpenOffice(v 2.0.3) onwards, Tamil language
> pack is made available by openoffice itself.
> You can find the Tamil language pack (ta-IN) in this URL:
> http://oootranslation.services.openoffice.org/pub/OpenOffice.org/2.0.3rc7/
>
> Steps to install tamil pack:
> 1. Install english version of OpenOffice.org 2.0.3 first (you can get it
> from http://download.openoffice.org/2.0.3/index.html )
>
> 2. Download and install the tamil language pack for your OS (seperate
> language pack is available for linux/windows & Solaris) from
> http://oootranslation.services.openoffice.org/pub/OpenOffice.org/2.0.3rc7/
>
> 3. Open the openoffice.org , go to
> Tools --> Options --> Language Settings --> Languages
> There there we can choose the Language of "User Interface".  Here Choose
> Tamil,
>
> 4. Close OpenOffice and open again. now you should be able to see the
> interface in tamil.
>
> Please try and let us know if it works fine in Linspire..
>

> I think we have to use cross platform compilers like mingw instead of gcc.

MinGW is the windows port (sort of) of GCC in case you don't know.
So, cross compiling for Windows from GNU/Linux requires MinGW.

From girish1729 at yahoo.com  Thu Jul 20 05:12:24 2006
From: girish1729 at yahoo.com (Girish Venkatachalam)
Date: Thu Jul 20 17:42:52 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] How to build firefox with indic support
In-Reply-To: <6be355de0607200444i1774b7c2gdcdda680dd8a7710@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20060720121224.9296.qmail@web35605.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

--- Narayanan Srinivasan <sri.narayanan@gmail.com>
wrote:

> hi i was trying to build this. i had about 3 GB
> before starting the build.
> this is what happened before the build aborted :(

3 GB of RAM? You must be kidding. I think your machine
is not setup with adequate swap space. I compiled
firefox 1.5 with 256 MB RAM and my swap is 700 MB.

Now that your machine is setup, if you have
partitioned properly according to standard
recommendation, I suggest you mv files from a
partition and convert it into a swap partition with
mkswap and swapon commands. 
Remember this is a dangerous surgery and you have to
be very careful. 

*If not it will screw up your disk and you will lose
all data. You are warned.*

Standard disclaimers apply. :-)

Also you have to add entry in /etc/fstab, reboot and
check with top whether ur swap is properly recognized.


But it is worthwhile to do this as without swap your
machine will gasp for breath even if you run firefox. 

If you are too scared to do this, backup and reinstall
with 1 GB swap. Doesn't hurt. 

HTH,
Girish

From srini.it at gmail.com  Fri Jul 21 11:25:18 2006
From: srini.it at gmail.com (Srinivasan Sundararajan)
Date: Fri Jul 21 11:27:05 2006
Subject: [Ilugc] Open Source Projects at Engg Clgs, Fear or Lack of Time
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0607211018150.7075-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
References: <a54a308e0607202139l9b216doac67065fbfb9afab@mail.gmail.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.44.0607211018150.7075-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
Message-ID: <328077850607202255n2d39df6ek82ae354aaf035813@mail.gmail.com>

hello everybody:
Linux-based projects (part of them using only open source tools, rest mainly
java-based) have been done by many students. Some of the colleges have
developed open source based applications and are using them in-house. In
most the cases, there are HoDs/Lecturers who are enthusiastic and
knowledgeable enough to assist the students.

We can talk to the HOD concerned (and other HoD), offer them project ideas,
provide mentor support. Already, the teacher group which came for NRCFOSS
training programs have given various project titles. Kenneth is driving the
whole action -- please see nrcfosshelpline.org.

Many students start thinking about the project in october, contact companies
in november, start reading / learning in december and work only for one
month, viz. Jan. Thereafter, they have to come back to colleges for theory
courses and project documentation. Even if they have 3 months, it is not
sufficient. [Some of my students had divided the project into 2 parts :
first part was presented as project report for the Anna Univ exam, after
their exams they went to the company and completed the project during
May-Jun-Jul. At AU-KBC a couple of groups of students have done in a similar
way. In Muthayammal College, the lectuer - Ms. Krishnaveni -- has got a
group of students who have just completed the degree willing to work on FOSS
projects].

We are now advising the lecturers to identify 1-2 student group per college,
give them project ideas and reference materials in Jul-Aug, so that they
could work in earnest during Nov-Jan. Our portal could be used as wiki /
repository, provided there is interest from students. Am willing to be in
touch with the concerned colleges/HoDs/Lectures to push the thing thru.
Whenever LUG/NRCFOSS visit the colleges, we can offer our assistance in this
regard.
We can ask them to send their initial queries to <nrcfoss@au-kbc.in> -- we
can then guide them to use wiki/repository.

Srinivasan.

NRC FOSS is supporting students to do FOSS Projects, provide mentors who 
can guide the students, provide all sorts of other assistance and the 
real bonaza is we have plans even to pay them for their projects 
(successfully completed and hosted in our  repos which can be used by 
anyone).

Actually this is a very good chance for students to try out their hands 
over FOSS based projects. Our wiki 
[http://nrcfosshelpline.in/code/wiki/ProjectIdeas] hosts few projects 
and students are welcomed to add more ideas. We would also be happy to 
work with ilugc (as it is always :) ) in this manner.

As Raman said, you can ask your niece to contact their HOD. We will have 
a formal session in their coll for taking FOSS based projects, have some 
GLVs and LDDs also.

Senior System Administrator

Responsibilities

      * Design, configure and maintain a data center for an On Demand
        enterprise software environment
        
      * Evaluate and recommend appropriate Open Source products for On
        Demand deployment
        


Required Skills/Experience 

      * Experience solving challenging technical problems in a
        production setting  
        
      * Participated in the entire lifecycle (architecture, planning,
        deployment, maintenance) of Linux-based enterprise services  
        
      * Strong hands-on knowledge in configuring, securing,
        troubleshooting Linux-based network services (e.g., mail, Web,
        file-serving) and protocols (e.g., SMTP, IMAP, DNS, FTP, HTTP)
        
      * Proficient in different Open Source products  
        
      * Well versed in one or more scripting languages ? Perl, PHP, Unix
        Shell  
        
      * Database administration is a plus
        
      * 3-5 years of system administration experience a must
        
      * Growing and mentoring teams from ground zero and startup
        experience are a plus
        
      * Excellent communication skills, planning and attention to
        details are a must
        
      * Computer Science or equivalent degree preferred.

Subject: [Ilugc] Another Localized GNU/Linux is Out - Nepalinux
Message-ID: <44C0CE47.6030705@gmail.com>

Hi all,
I remember a post about Dzongkha Debian in this mailing list. Just now I 
got to see another such initiative, this time from Nepal called as 
Nepalinux [http://nepalinux.org/]. Its great to see small countries like 
  Nepal coming out with such a Open Source initiative, but why not such 
things happening in India. I am intending to mean that nothing happens 
in India, but I feel we are a but sluggish. Why don't each state come up 
with a localized version so that installing localization support is not 
an issue and regional languages are available on fly. Correct me if am 
wrong, but this shows low level of awareness about localized FOSS 
softwares in India ;)

-- 
With Regards

Parthan ('technofreak')

From prasannadavid at gmail.com  Fri Jul 21 09:50:55 2006
From: prasannadavid at gmail.com (Prasanna David G)

In-Reply-To: <44C0CE47.6030705@gmail.com>
